{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"MAD Skills Gradle and AGP build APIs Wrap Up!","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/12/mad-skills-gradle-and-agp-build-apis.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgo1Fw61B9qtQESKdVJzcNXOG0RzhA2k85zkDMDNidBiQY7B6uguHXQ9t9IPB9BiHS0WTB1b4fwIgeN5zEIJrmznF9pt5lu9186wvXxJ3IKfLi8Fci8LyMDbQKGYc7nnijJ9_lhrNHtRQamaF2GTSXyJq5_lQk7we3cSfSviOxhgKN9TscMJaGgdMZJ\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgo1Fw61B9qtQESKdVJzcNXOG0RzhA2k85zkDMDNidBiQY7B6uguHXQ9t9IPB9BiHS0WTB1b4fwIgeN5zEIJrmznF9pt5lu9186wvXxJ3IKfLi8Fci8LyMDbQKGYc7nnijJ9_lhrNHtRQamaF2GTSXyJq5_lQk7we3cSfSviOxhgKN9TscMJaGgdMZJ\"> <p><em>Posted by Murat Yener, Android Developer Advocate</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgo1Fw61B9qtQESKdVJzcNXOG0RzhA2k85zkDMDNidBiQY7B6uguHXQ9t9IPB9BiHS0WTB1b4fwIgeN5zEIJrmznF9pt5lu9186wvXxJ3IKfLi8Fci8LyMDbQKGYc7nnijJ9_lhrNHtRQamaF2GTSXyJq5_lQk7we3cSfSviOxhgKN9TscMJaGgdMZJ\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"MAD Skills graphic\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgo1Fw61B9qtQESKdVJzcNXOG0RzhA2k85zkDMDNidBiQY7B6uguHXQ9t9IPB9BiHS0WTB1b4fwIgeN5zEIJrmznF9pt5lu9186wvXxJ3IKfLi8Fci8LyMDbQKGYc7nnijJ9_lhrNHtRQamaF2GTSXyJq5_lQk7we3cSfSviOxhgKN9TscMJaGgdMZJ\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <br> <p> That’s a wrap! We’ve just finished a new MAD skills series on Gradle and Android Gradle plugin build APIs. In this series we shifted gears and took a look at how you can extend your build by using Gradle and brand new Android Gradle plugin APIs. </p> <p> We covered how Gradle works, how you can configure the Android Gradle plugin, and learned which APIs to use to help customize your builds and keep your builds fast and efficient. If you missed this series or some of the episodes, here is a quick recap of what to expect. </p> <h3>Episode 1: Configure your build - Intro to Gradle and AGP </h3> <p> Gradle is a general purpose build tool which can build specific project types by using plugins. Plugins introduce a way to configure the build and decide which tasks are needed to build that project. Gradle configures and executes these tasks in different phases. Understanding how the build phases work and how to configure the Android Gradle plugin can help you customize your build according to your project’s needs and keep build times efficient. </p> <p> You can check out the following video or if you prefer, read the <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/gradle-and-agp-build-apis-configure-your-build-9a10db5b2262\">article</a>. </p> \n     <center>\n      <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/mk0XBWenod8\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n     </center> <br> <h3>Episode 2: How to write a plugin</h3> <p> Extending your build by writing your own plugin gives you a way to customize your build even further! Starting with version 7.0, Android Gradle Plugin now offers stable extension points for manipulating variant configuration and the produced build artifacts. In this episode we started with writing a custom task and used the new Variant API to initialize and modify properties of Variants. </p> \n      <center>\n       <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/LPzBVtwGxlo\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n      </center> <p> You can find the same content in <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/gradle-and-agp-build-apis-how-to-write-a-plugin-1695b590e4ec\">article</a> form. </p> <br> <h3>Episode 3: Taking your plugin to the next step</h3> <p> As we saw in previous episodes, keeping your config phase fast and resolving values lazily can help keep your builds efficient. Providers and Properties let you pass inputs and receive outputs from Gradle tasks lazily. In this episode we also take a look at the new Artifacts API to access and modify the app manifest. </p> <p> Check out the <a href=\"https://medium.com/androiddevelopers/gradle-and-agp-build-apis-taking-your-plugin-to-the-next-step-95e7bd1cd4c9\">article</a> or the following video. </p> \n       <center>\n        <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/SB4QlngQQW0\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe>\n       </center> <br> <h3>Episode 4: Gradle and AGP Build APIs Community Tip </h3> <p> In the last episode in the series, we feature Alex Saveau, who maintains the Gradle Play Publisher and Version Orchestrator plugins. Alex shares a tip on using modern AGP and Gradle APIs to manipulate Android build artifacts. </p> <p> To learn more, check out the following video. </p> \n        <center>\n         <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/8SFfffaB0CU\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n        </center> <br> <h3>Episode 6: Live Q&amp;A</h3> <p> Finally, we wrapped up this series with a live Q&amp;A session where we answered your questions. views","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/discontinuing-kotlin-synthetics-for-views.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/zsmb13\">Márton Braun</a>, Developer Relations Engineer</em><p> <br> \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEggUWTxbYc5S2Mb6uquoCZSnzMI7lAusH5pY2Ml25N3RA59hie24M1PyxTavvJn1UfSE5kgsD8kwZZLS3Htrthfs2XJCcBVtCxlJGOXq7KIXNyahmQseEjzFVrwcJYFjpav-1PB39BpC9jxxWrM5unZVU50VzK08KaKbZ2YeVeKqfghluQaBM3gXOze\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"ALT TEXT GOES HERE\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEggUWTxbYc5S2Mb6uquoCZSnzMI7lAusH5pY2Ml25N3RA59hie24M1PyxTavvJn1UfSE5kgsD8kwZZLS3Htrthfs2XJCcBVtCxlJGOXq7KIXNyahmQseEjzFVrwcJYFjpav-1PB39BpC9jxxWrM5unZVU50VzK08KaKbZ2YeVeKqfghluQaBM3gXOze\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>&nbsp;\n     </center> <p> Synthetic properties to access views were created as a way to eliminate the common boilerplate of <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/android/view/View#findviewbyid\">findViewById</a></code> calls. These synthetics are provided by JetBrains in the <a href=\"https://plugins.gradle.org/plugin/org.jetbrains.kotlin.android.extensions\">Kotlin Android Extensions Gradle plugin</a> (not to be confused with <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin/ktx\">Android KTX</a>). <p> In November 2020, <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2020/11/the-future-of-kotlin-android-extensions.html\">we announced that this plugin has been deprecated</a> in favor of better solutions, and we recommended removing the plugin from your projects. We know many developers still depend on this plugin’s features, and we’ve extended the support timeframe so you have more time to complete your migrations. </p> <p> We are now setting a deadline for these migrations: <strong>the plugin will be removed in Kotlin 1.8</strong>, which is expected to be released by the <strong>end of 2022</strong>. At that time, you won’t be able to update your project to newer Kotlin versions if it still depends on the Kotlin Android Extensions plugin. This means that now is the time to perform the necessary migrations in your projects. </p> <p> Instead of synthetics, we recommend using <strong><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/libraries/view-binding\">View Binding</a></strong>, which generates type-safe binding classes from XML layout files. These bindings provide convenient access to view references and they work safely for layouts with multiple configurations. See the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/topic/libraries/view-binding/migration\">migration guide</a> for detailed instructions on how to adopt View Binding. If you encounter any issues, you can <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=843972&amp;template=1414794\">report a bug on the Issue Tracker</a>. </p> <p> <em>When building <strong>new features</strong>, consider using <strong><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a></strong>, Android's modern UI toolkit. Layouts built with Compose are declarative Kotlin code, eliminating the need to work with view references.</em> </p> <p> Another feature included in the plugin is <strong>Parcelize</strong>, which helps you create parcelable classes. Parcelize is now available in the standalone <code>kotlin-parcelize</code> plugin with unchanged functionality. To get up and running with the new plugin, check out the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin/parcelize\">Parcelize documentation page</a>. </p> <p> If you’re still using the Kotlin Android Extensions Gradle plugin, kick off your migration in time so that you can keep upgrading to new Kotlin releases in the future. This will enable you to use the latest language features and take advantage of tooling and compiler improvements. </p>\n      <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n       <a Developers","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhxtjouMCgk8sv8wkvC5Aip4muxMo4TLnfSVtZ3Hw7ZpuqXQmk-EkV9qk9PKim0yVFVFlpjEJG-vqh6gCLFkQPuf2dQk6qEdQZM_9brvuxBA0dtOUlvUh7tMIQsF11RnSnSPWOPKDIzeiixfapL2ax4YgMahJppgG_a5rjs_4QBjzzgzqsDs9Wc-Ldx":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn30@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-26-40-767_306046dc8295610a.webp","https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEggUWTxbYc5S2Mb6uquoCZSnzMI7lAusH5pY2Ml25N3RA59hie24M1PyxTavvJn1UfSE5kgsD8kwZZLS3Htrthfs2XJCcBVtCxlJGOXq7KIXNyahmQseEjzFVrwcJYFjpav-1PB39BpC9jxxWrM5unZVU50VzK08KaKbZ2YeVeKqfghluQaBM3gXOze":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn36@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-26-48-615_f9fff2d6026b9914.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn7@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-26-47-709_e6aa4d73b74f71ed.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?i=OJDFq4IzgKE:GO3MDNTM5ig:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn21@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-26-47-758_650b12f310b63790.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647246393386},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 #IamaGDE","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/12/creating-app-to-help-your-community.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgHl1OMxu_r7B6C2OHY0OsAyNn8j00v_A2ASjMKfjrw2JO0B9fbD6-5uohhucBeSLh_6ngRqhyARan_Tn1Sd-veSxOc3b-Lo1H_Q0PktyH5hrpCkhX54T8PoLWqFlfkRWIIy_0GWkK84s1CgfSk8w05GanB28I5mnb4vDPrHqG0CBmkcNuiqNygPjgP\"> src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgHl1OMxu_r7B6C2OHY0OsAyNn8j00v_A2ASjMKfjrw2JO0B9fbD6-5uohhucBeSLh_6ngRqhyARan_Tn1Sd-veSxOc3b-Lo1H_Q0PktyH5hrpCkhX54T8PoLWqFlfkRWIIy_0GWkK84s1CgfSk8w05GanB28I5mnb4vDPrHqG0CBmkcNuiqNygPjgP\"> <p><em>Posted by Alicja Heisig, Developer Relations Program Manager</em><p> <p> <em>Welcome to #IamaGDE - a series of spotlights presenting Google Developer Experts (GDEs) from across the globe. Discover their stories, passions, and highlights of their community work.</em> </p> <p> Gaston Saillen started coding for fun, making apps for his friends. About seven years ago, he began working full-time as an <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/\">Android developer</a> for startups. He built a bunch of apps—and then someone gave him an idea for an app that has had a broad social impact in his local community. Now, he is a senior Android developer at Distillery. </p> <h2>Meet Gaston Saillen, Google Developer Expert in Android and Firebase.</h2> \n    <center>\n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgHl1OMxu_r7B6C2OHY0OsAyNn8j00v_A2ASjMKfjrw2JO0B9fbD6-5uohhucBeSLh_6ngRqhyARan_Tn1Sd-veSxOc3b-Lo1H_Q0PktyH5hrpCkhX54T8PoLWqFlfkRWIIy_0GWkK84s1CgfSk8w05GanB28I5mnb4vDPrHqG0CBmkcNuiqNygPjgP\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Photo of Gaston\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1428\" data-original-width=\"1999\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgHl1OMxu_r7B6C2OHY0OsAyNn8j00v_A2ASjMKfjrw2JO0B9fbD6-5uohhucBeSLh_6ngRqhyARan_Tn1Sd-veSxOc3b-Lo1H_Q0PktyH5hrpCkhX54T8PoLWqFlfkRWIIy_0GWkK84s1CgfSk8w05GanB28I5mnb4vDPrHqG0CBmkcNuiqNygPjgP\" /></a>\n     </div>\n    </center> <h2>Building the Uh-LaLa! app</h2> <p> After seven years of building apps for startups, Gaston visited a local food delivery truck to pick up dinner, and the server asked him, “Why don’t you do a food delivery app for the town, since you are an Android developer? We don’t have any food delivery apps here, but in the big city, there are tons of them.” </p> <p> The food truck proprietor added that he was new in town and needed a tool to boost his sales. Gaston was up for the challenge and created a straightforward delivery app for local Cordoba restaurants he named <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.uhlala&amp;hl=en_US&amp;gl=US\">Uh-Lala!</a> Restaurants configure the app themselves, and there’s no app fee. “My plan was to deliver this service to this community and start making some progress on the technology that they use for delivery,” says Gaston. “And after that, a lot of other food delivery services started using the app.” </p> <p> The base app is built similarly to food delivery apps for bigger companies. Gaston built it for Cordoba restaurants first, after several months of development, and it’s still the only food delivery app in town. When he released the app, it immediately got traction, with people placing orders. His friends joined, and the app expanded. “I’ve made a lot of apps as an Android engineer, but this is the first time I’ve made one that had such an impact on my community.” </p> <p> He had to figure out how to deliver real-time notifications that food was ready for delivery. “That was a little tough at first, but then I got to know more about all the backend functions and everything, and that opened up a lot of new features.” </p> <p> He also had to educate two groups of users: Restaurant owners need to know how to input their data into the app, and customers had to change their habit of using their phones for calls instead of apps. </p> <p> Gaston says seeing people using the app is rewarding because he feels like he’s helping his community.<strong> </strong>“All of a sudden, nearby towns started using Uh-LaLa!, and I didn't expect it to grow that big, and it helped those communities.” </p> <p> During the COVID-19 pandemic, many restaurants struggled to maintain their sales numbers. A local pub owner ran a promotion through Instagram to use the Uh-Lala! App for ten percent off, and their sales returned to pre-COVID levels. “That is a success story. They were really happy about the app.” </p> \n    <center>\n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEj9UGlzL9GAm2yLhG9uS-uzYBE4Xp-NOwUPpEVt1awufKABXR_BxYF1s2bH8OF_VAwguVNbmrYaT1HU-yG1SByUO0y0WLSSVZczYfW_CMM4zvJhH820t4ewPvhkeO5UbvoyPfspK63Ktx_AGwJkuJDH-HGcGaC20V7XMHsmpH_8ITrfmwAAZGUrJJex\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"image of person holding a phone and an image of an app on the phone\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1132\" data-original-width=\"2280\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEj9UGlzL9GAm2yLhG9uS-uzYBE4Xp-NOwUPpEVt1awufKABXR_BxYF1s2bH8OF_VAwguVNbmrYaT1HU-yG1SByUO0y0WLSSVZczYfW_CMM4zvJhH820t4ewPvhkeO5UbvoyPfspK63Ktx_AGwJkuJDH-HGcGaC20V7XMHsmpH_8ITrfmwAAZGUrJJex\" /></a>\n     </div>\n    </center> <br> <h2>Becoming a GDE</h2> <p> Gaston has been a GDE for seven years. When he was working on his last startup, he found himself regularly answering questions about <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/\">Android development</a> and <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/\">Firebase</a> on <a href=\"http://stackoverflow.com\">StackOverflow</a> and creating developer content in the form of blog posts and YouTube videos. When he learned about the GDE program, it seemed like a perfect way to continue to contribute his Android development knowledge to an even broader developer community. Once he was selected, he continued writing blog posts and making videos—and now, they reach a broader audience. </p> <p> “I created <a href=\"https://www.udemy.com/course/curso-definitivo-para-aprender-a-programar-en-android/\">a course on Udemy</a> that I keep updated, and I’m still writing the blog posts,” he says. “We also started the GDG here in Cordoba, and we try to have a new talk every month.” </p> <p> Gaston enjoys the GDE community and sharing his ideas about Firebase and Android with other developers. He and several fellow Firebase developers started a WhatsApp group to chat about Firebase. “I enjoy being a Google Developer Expert because I can meet members of the community that do the same things that I do. It’s a really nice way to keep improving my skills and meet other people who also contribute and make videos and blogs about what I love: Android.” </p> <p> The Android platform provides developers with state-of-the art tools to build apps for user. Firebase allows developers to accelerate and scale app development without managing infrastructure; release apps and monitor their performance and stability; and boost engagement with analytics, A/B testing, and messaging campaigns. </p> \n     <center>\n      <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n       <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh55RfLIAX4ET7uEjTWOgahCtkDO6nigM-cpzAtR5ToIGo_JxAiRKzhkOkVlJyu8DKiDA9AkbZMOSDfFCWfgzGxXWmwNCy_UMVaZZoJOa8JC90tNDRPM_reaEspOvIhcguusfOmz_vZ_XQhubokforAQOaMEdVnBAlUq50HyNcYLrXM1KYdAfwFOlea\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"photo of a webpage in another language\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1023\" data-original-width=\"1999\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh55RfLIAX4ET7uEjTWOgahCtkDO6nigM-cpzAtR5ToIGo_JxAiRKzhkOkVlJyu8DKiDA9AkbZMOSDfFCWfgzGxXWmwNCy_UMVaZZoJOa8JC90tNDRPM_reaEspOvIhcguusfOmz_vZ_XQhubokforAQOaMEdVnBAlUq50HyNcYLrXM1KYdAfwFOlea\" /></a>\n      </div>\n     </center> <br> <h2>Future plans</h2> <p> Gaston looks forward to developing Uh-La-La further and building more apps, like a coworking space reservation app that would show users the hours and locations of nearby coworking spaces and allow them to reserve a space at a certain time. He is also busy as an Android developer with Distillery. </p> \n      <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n       <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEge78Jue1aA-b8RUS3hPVO9eVe3vdsxfhY4-U-gmsnSdxYFi54N8EQtBSrcjTVCYSDy5zgBrcpRKaKFk-I_MR3iIwY-0emoKnW5Ya4ABCw2zeJ-pXstcYiV7IRPrASmufyrOCa3Rt32x7f0FFEHhXfSI1RNIGfW24t4ix974iUcmOz8zgix5ro3Bp35\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Photo of Gaston on a telelvision show\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"992\" data-original-width=\"1824\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEge78Jue1aA-b8RUS3hPVO9eVe3vdsxfhY4-U-gmsnSdxYFi54N8EQtBSrcjTVCYSDy5zgBrcpRKaKFk-I_MR3iIwY-0emoKnW5Ya4ABCw2zeJ-pXstcYiV7IRPrASmufyrOCa3Rt32x7f0FFEHhXfSI1RNIGfW24t4ix974iUcmOz8zgix5ro3Bp35\" /></a>\n      </div> <br> <h2>Gaston’s advice to future developers</h2> <p> “Keep moving forward. Any adversity that you will be having in your career will be part of your learning, so the more that you find problems and solve them, the more that you will learn and progress in your career.” </p> 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Freeing up 60% of storage for apps ","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/03/freeing-up-60-of-storage-for-apps.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhAba1fyHq6ddgUfT09YxU3XkAhnolKyLnXE2GmcJABVT-y8PWLKUiC7LmesY7Txak65fc6nW8T7yar9_4Uz4ezcBA_MDZ-yqBR2cj4ipSN-5l_E57exa3m9qt2MHFo_RdLWc_YDX7J7AOMkyzs43ylbGtwl6Z8GSf1zgs71Te36cQ-9Z_qgMgFroLq\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhAba1fyHq6ddgUfT09YxU3XkAhnolKyLnXE2GmcJABVT-y8PWLKUiC7LmesY7Txak65fc6nW8T7yar9_4Uz4ezcBA_MDZ-yqBR2cj4ipSN-5l_E57exa3m9qt2MHFo_RdLWc_YDX7J7AOMkyzs43ylbGtwl6Z8GSf1zgs71Te36cQ-9Z_qgMgFroLq\"> <p><em>Posted by Lidia Gaymond and Vicki Amin, Product Managers at Google Play</em><p> <p> One of the main reasons users uninstall apps is to free up space. To prevent unnecessary uninstalls and help users get more out of their devices, we started working on a new feature that would enable app archiving. </p> <p> Archiving is a new functionality that will allow users to reclaim ~60% of app storage temporarily by removing parts of the app rather than uninstalling it completely. An archived app will remain on the device and can easily be restored to the latest available compatible version, whilst preserving the user data. </p> <p> With the release of the upcoming version of <a href=\"https://github.com/google/bundletool/releases\">Bundletool</a> 1.10, we are taking the first step toward making archiving available to all developers using App Bundles. For apps built with the Android Gradle Plugin 7.3, we will start generating a new type of APK - archived APKs. Archived APKs are very small APKs that preserve user data until the app is restored. <strong>While we will start creating archived APKs now, they won’t be functional until the archiving functionality is launched to consumers later in the year. </strong> </p> <p> Once launched, archiving will deliver great benefits to both users and developers. Instead of uninstalling an app, users would be able to “archive” it - free up space temporarily and be able to re-activate the app quickly and easily. Developers can benefit from fewer uninstalls and substantially lower friction to pick back up with their favourite apps. </p> <p> As before, all APKs generated will be available to download and inspect through <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/android-publisher/download-apks\">Generated APKs API</a> or in Play Console under <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/about/app-bundle-explorer/\">App Bundle Explorer</a>. Since the functionality is open source, developers will be able to inspect the code, and other app stores can benefit from it too. </p> <p> If you want to opt-out of the generation of archived APKs, you can modify the build.gradle file of the project: </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">android {\n    bundle {\n        storeArchive {\n            enable = false\n        }\n    }\n}</pre> <p> Alternatively, if you are not using Gradle to build your apps, you can opt-out with a new option in the BundleConfig: </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">{\n  \"optimizations\": {\n    \"storeArchive\": {\n      \"enabled\": false\n    }\n  }\n}</pre> <p> Keep an eye out for more information about app archiving on the Android Developers blog. </p>\n    <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n     <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=Cdgf6Qs5hrc:kGURcWSGUl4:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n     <a <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/dagalpin?lang=en\">Dan Galpin</a>, Developer Relations Engineer</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgLyiqpYgjYxkUGwd4i_axPqdGgRRe8wuOmOwTOFtDoC7Iziv1rePgNLGYlCT6OR1fRW7vl7u8ayH7Dwr-lkdrl_eAssko1VX45rsR9tXlrR-s5yhqAkuf0-SoTxZahF1d0CSwFvLKlFSeXIWpZ2rpAslqHYSCS2Vu7y1SwztjLgZkFnyEJk7eVt6kO\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android robot on a pretend video call\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgLyiqpYgjYxkUGwd4i_axPqdGgRRe8wuOmOwTOFtDoC7Iziv1rePgNLGYlCT6OR1fRW7vl7u8ayH7Dwr-lkdrl_eAssko1VX45rsR9tXlrR-s5yhqAkuf0-SoTxZahF1d0CSwFvLKlFSeXIWpZ2rpAslqHYSCS2Vu7y1SwztjLgZkFnyEJk7eVt6kO\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n    </center> <p>In October of 2021 we released the final unit of <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/courses/android-basics-kotlin/course\">Android Basics in Kotlin</a>, our free, self-paced programming course that makes Android development accessible to everyone. It teaches people with no programming experience how to build Android apps. Along the way, students learn the fundamentals of programming and the basics of the Kotlin programming language. </p> <p> In response to feedback from educators and learners, we've continued to iterate on our course material, adding projects that allow you to apply learnings along with new topics that can prepare students for more advanced material. </p> <h3>A focus on basics</h3> <p> With these updates, Android Basics in Kotlin now covers the key material covered in Android Kotlin Fundamentals, so we will be sunsetting the latter course. More advanced learners are encouraged to work through the Basics material, skipping sections that they are familiar with and moving straight to quizzes. Focusing on basics means that intermediate and advanced learners that might be missing a key concept will have what they need to succeed with this material. This also allows our team to focus on making sure our courseware continues to represent our most recent guidance. In addition to courseware, we're continuing to provide codelabs, code samples, documentation, and video content to serve learners at all levels. </p> <h3>What's next?</h3> <p> Our team is hard at work on the next course that will teach people how to program Android applications using Jetpack Compose. We're looking forward to teaching Android’s modern toolkit for building native UI because of all the ways that it simplifies and accelerates Android UI development. </p> <h3>What to do now</h3> <p> Taking the current course will teach you the fundamentals of app development, serving as a great starting point should you want to explore the existing <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/courses/pathways/compose\">Jetpack Compose Learning Pathway</a>, or jump into the upcoming Android Basics with Compose course. You'll have a foundation that you can build on as you continue to explore the world of Android development. Both versions of Android Basics are planned to coexist, giving the option of learning Android with either UI toolkit. </p> <p> Whether you’ve never built an app before but want to learn how, or just want to brush up on some of our latest best practices, check out the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/courses/android-basics-kotlin/course\">Android Basics in Kotlin course</a>. </p> \n    <div 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Improving App Performance with Baseline Profiles","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/01/improving-app-performance-with-baseline.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" /> \n<img src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEicCVDoRaflBAdKr9_Zh2cAGUB8pphAj9m0w1iN7VLizNZ6L2iNGNSnt7tvD6MP72BW8eqobZpU751t32aF47bpNDv2walZ6zzsXxyuAjCyhBl0b4o06X1j3bPi0AAU0EedqYjp5FSXMQHHzvxBedjsST3MIIFvalX3tZpgiFZgEdqbB2f_H741Irrb\" style=\"display: none;\" /> \n<em><h3>Or how to improve startup time by up to 40%</h3></em> \n<p><em>Posted by Kateryna Semenova, DevRel Engineer; Rahul Ravikumar, Software Engineer; Chris Craik, Software Engineer </em></p> \n<center> \n <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEicCVDoRaflBAdKr9_Zh2cAGUB8pphAj9m0w1iN7VLizNZ6L2iNGNSnt7tvD6MP72BW8eqobZpU751t32aF47bpNDv2walZ6zzsXxyuAjCyhBl0b4o06X1j3bPi0AAU0EedqYjp5FSXMQHHzvxBedjsST3MIIFvalX3tZpgiFZgEdqbB2f_H741Irrb\"><img alt=\"ALT TEXT GOES HERE\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"714\" data-original-width=\"1058\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEicCVDoRaflBAdKr9_Zh2cAGUB8pphAj9m0w1iN7VLizNZ6L2iNGNSnt7tvD6MP72BW8eqobZpU751t32aF47bpNDv2walZ6zzsXxyuAjCyhBl0b4o06X1j3bPi0AAU0EedqYjp5FSXMQHHzvxBedjsST3MIIFvalX3tZpgiFZgEdqbB2f_H741Irrb\" style=\"width: 100%;\" /></a>\n</center>\n<p></p>\n<p></p> \n<br> <h2>Why is startup time important?</h2> <p> A lot of apps find correlation between app performance and user engagement. People expect apps to be <strong>responsive</strong> and <strong>fast</strong> to load. <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/9844486\">Startup time</a> is one of the major metrics for app performance and quality. </p> <p> Some of our partners have already invested a lot of time and resources for app startup optimizations. For example, check out the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/11/improving-app-startup-facebook-app.html\">Facebook</a> story. </p> <p> In this blog post we’ll discuss <strong>Baseline Profiles</strong> and how they improve app and library performance, including startup time <strong>by up to 40%</strong>. While this blogpost focuses on startup, baseline profiles also significantly improve jank as well. </p> <br> <h2>History</h2> <p> Android 9 (API level 28) introduced <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2019/04/improving-app-performance-with-art.html\">ART optimizing profiles in Play Cloud</a> to improve app startup time. On average, we’ve seen that apps' cold starts are at least 15% faster across a variety of devices when Cloud Profiles are available. </p> <br> <strong>How do Profiles work? </strong> <p> When the app is first launched after install or update, its code runs in an interpreted mode until it is <a href=\"https://source.android.com/devices/tech/dalvik/jit-compiler\">JIT</a>ted. In an APK, Java and Kotlin code is compiled as dex bytecode, but not fully compiled to machine code (since Android 6), due to the cost of storing and loading fully compiled apps. Classes and methods that are frequently used in the app, as well as those used for app startup, are recorded into a profile file. Once the device enters idle mode, <a href=\"https://source.android.com/devices/tech/dalvik/configure%23how_art_works\">ART</a> compiles the apps based on these profiles. This speeds up subsequent app launches. </p> <p> Starting with Android 9 (API level 28), Google Play also provides Cloud Profiles. When an app runs on a device, the profiles generated by ART are uploaded by the Play Store app and aggregated in the cloud. Once there are enough profiles uploaded for an application, the Play app uses the aggregated profile for subsequent installs. </p> <br> <h2>Problem</h2> <p> While Cloud Profiles are great when they are available, they aren't always ready to be used when an app is installed. Collecting and aggregating the profiles usually takes several days, which is a problem when many apps update on a weekly basis. Many users will install an update before the Cloud Profile is available. The Google Android team started looking for other ways to improve the latency of profiles. </p> <br> <h2>Solution</h2> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/profile/baselineprofiles\">Baseline Profiles</a> are a new mechanism to provide profiles which can be used on Android 7 (API level 24) and higher. A baseline profile is an ART profile generated by the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/releases/gradle-plugin\">Android Gradle plugin</a> using a human readable profile format that can be provided by apps and libraries. An example might look like this: </p> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">HSPLandroidx/compose/runtime/ComposerImpl;-&gt;updateValue(Ljava/lang/Object;)V\nHSPLandroidx/compose/runtime/ComposerImpl;-&gt;updatedNodeCount(I)I\nHLandroidx/compose/runtime/ComposerImpl;-&gt;validateNodeExpected()V\nPLandroidx/compose/runtime/CompositionImpl;-&gt;applyChanges()V\nHLandroidx/compose/runtime/ComposerKt;-&gt;findLocation(Ljava/util/List;I)I\n</pre>\n     <center>\n      <p id=\"imgCaption\">Example for Compose library.</p>\n     </center> <br> <p> The binary profile is stored in a specific location in the APK assets directory (assets/dexopt/baseline.prof). </p> <p> Baseline Profiles are created during build time, shipped as part of the APK to Play, and then sent from Play to users when an app is downloaded. They fill the gap in the ART Cloud Profile pipeline, when Cloud Profiles are not yet available, and automatically merge with Cloud Profiles when they are. </p> <br> \n       <center> \n        <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiJCD60kr4b2awlU0dGuq7dpD_tcZowus0_97jcZrNwwHQCca7vnAp-8NGQTdR3BR7i0I5hOyh-sw87g-nirNExo6anRjKOpWKfjXsBDy8OIlO02pww5QlGwG7Z_QmZpJYxeP_ZgsKy5mqN2TV4yNc14XzjaP61hoWA81jRvm8cW9i3CT7O56KtmQhK\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"This diagram displays the baseline profile workflow from creation through end-user delivery.\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiJCD60kr4b2awlU0dGuq7dpD_tcZowus0_97jcZrNwwHQCca7vnAp-8NGQTdR3BR7i0I5hOyh-sw87g-nirNExo6anRjKOpWKfjXsBDy8OIlO02pww5QlGwG7Z_QmZpJYxeP_ZgsKy5mqN2TV4yNc14XzjaP61hoWA81jRvm8cW9i3CT7O56KtmQhK\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n        <p id=\"imgCaption\">This diagram displays the baseline profile workflow from creation through end-user delivery.</p>\n       </center> <br> <p> One of the biggest benefits of Baseline Profiles is that they can be developed and evaluated <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/profile/baselineprofiles#creating-profile-rules\">locally</a> so developers can see realistic end-user performance improvements. They are also supported on a lower version of Android(7 and higher) than Cloud Profiles, which are only available starting in Android 9. </p> <br> <h2>Impact </h2> <br> <strong>App devs</strong> <p> In early 2021, Google Maps switched from a two-week to a one-week release cycle. More frequent updates meant more frequently discarding local pre-compilation, and more users experiencing slow launches without Play Cloud Profiles. By using Baseline Profiles, Google Maps <strong>improved their average startup time by 30% </strong>and saw a corresponding<strong> increase in searches by 2.4%</strong>, an immense gain for such an established app. </p> <br> <strong>Library devs</strong> <p> Code in a library is just like that of an app - it's not fully compiled by default, which can be a problem if it does significant work on the critical path of startup. </p> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a> is a UI library that is not a part of the Android system image and thus not fully compiled when installed, unlike much of the Android View toolkit code. This was causing performance problems, especially for the first few cold launches of the app. </p> <p> To solve this problem, Compose <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/ergonomics#profile-inst\">uses profile installer</a>. It ships baseline profile rules which reduce startup time and jank in Compose apps. </p> <p> Google PlayStore’s search results page has been re-written with Compose. After incorporating the Baseline Profile rules from Compose, <strong>time to render the initial search results page with images improved by ~40%</strong>. </p> <p> The Android team has also added Baseline Profiles to relevant <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/\">AndroidX</a> libraries. This benefits all Android apps using these libraries. Constraint Layout has found <a href=\"https://github.com/androidx/constraintlayout/pull/423\">shipping profile rules</a> <strong>reduces animation frame times by more than one millisecond</strong>. </p> <br> <h2>How to use Baseline Profiles</h2> <p> <br> <strong>Create a custom Baseline Profile</strong> </br></p> <p> All apps and library developers can benefit from including Baseline Profiles. Ideally, developers create profiles for their most critical user journeys to ensure that those journeys have consistently fast performance regardless of whether cloud profiles are available. Check out the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/profile/baselineprofiles#creating-profile-rules\">detailed guide</a> on how to set up Baseline Profiles for both app and library developers. </p> <p> <br> <strong>Update dependencies</strong> </br></p> <p> If you are not ready to generate Baseline Profiles for your app right now, you can still benefit from them by updating your dependencies. If you build with Android Gradle Plugin 7.1.0-alpha05 or newer, you'll get Baseline Profiles included in your APK that are already provided by libraries (such as <a href=\"https://cs.android.com/search?q=baseline-prof.txt&amp;ss=androidx%2Fplatform%2Fframeworks%2Fsupport\">Jetpack</a>). Google Play compiles your app with these profiles at install time. You can supplement these profiles <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/profile/baselineprofiles#creating-profile-rules\">as part of building your application</a>. </p> <p> <br> <strong>Measure Improvements</strong> </br></p> <p> Don’t forget to measure improvements. Follow <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/profile/baselineprofiles#measuring-improvements\">the steps on how to measure startup</a> with the generated profile locally. </p> <br> <p> <strong>Provide feedback</strong> </p> <p>Please share <a href=\"https://b.corp.google.com/issues/new?component=1071684&amp;template=1592279\">your feedback and let us know your experience!</a></p>\n simple","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/01/announcing-glance-tiles-for-wear-os.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjo_CL5arSn2zb_YKP8hKjaMG3nqXXPQ_zn05X9FQ0XLdE2Ii6WeGG0eD_miObCRv2iz3hJ2T0lIIn3iDFyT3yN8B7NFET_fE5nhcw6MHQmOKK4G4R5XgXTkEIyqY4kjz2F5hpPscvQgsz0aRkVqSLynp-6x9HqkoldNYwDSp7kbttmh2JCW1cwUXhG\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjo_CL5arSn2zb_YKP8hKjaMG3nqXXPQ_zn05X9FQ0XLdE2Ii6WeGG0eD_miObCRv2iz3hJ2T0lIIn3iDFyT3yN8B7NFET_fE5nhcw6MHQmOKK4G4R5XgXTkEIyqY4kjz2F5hpPscvQgsz0aRkVqSLynp-6x9HqkoldNYwDSp7kbttmh2JCW1cwUXhG\"> <p><em>Posted by Anna Bernbaum, Associate Product Manager</em><p> <br> <p> Last year we announced the Wear <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/wear/tiles/package-summary\">Tiles API</a>. To complement that Java API, we are excited to announce that support for Wear OS Tiles has been added to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/glance\">Glance</a>, a new framework built on top of Jetpack Compose designed to make it easier to build for surfaces outside your app on Android. We'd love to get <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=1097239&amp;template=1611667\">your feedback</a> on this alpha version. </p> <p> Tiles provide Wear OS users easy access to the information and actions they need in order to get things done quickly. They also are one of the most used surfaces on Wear OS. Just one swipe away from the Watch Face, users can quickly access the most important information or actions from an app, like start a timer or get the latest weather forecast. </p> <br> \n      <center> \n       <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEja0lRP986r3FtVM21Rf4m8wzeVMYVjyEnBKGLcxTIaA7GhT_pMcyPYeh4h99EKiTiRT_1FwG5lZ55NldCtYY60mVDGkwi-VqcCV820b3sNmhP0FfJaqFZHbqbYonTGntbe7VAhd_ppkA4vPbcREizutdc-RAX6EruFZrKtYQgbYXPc7vXblrzh47SW\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:40%\" alt=\"Watch face gif\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/01/ https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEja0lRP986r3FtVM21Rf4m8wzeVMYVjyEnBKGLcxTIaA7GhT_pMcyPYeh4h99EKiTiRT_1FwG5lZ55NldCtYY60mVDGkwi-VqcCV820b3sNmhP0FfJaqFZHbqbYonTGntbe7VAhd_ppkA4vPbcREizutdc-RAX6EruFZrKtYQgbYXPc7vXblrzh47SW\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n      </center> <br> <br> <p> Let's see how we can create a Tile with Glance: </p> <br> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">class HelloTileService : GlanceTileService() {\n   @Composable\n   override fun Content() {\n       Text(text = \"Hello Glance\")\n   }\n}</pre> <br> <p> The simple code above generates the Tile below. </p> <br> \n           <center> \n            <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEinOIEmuVkJHM4htJKvBcFh4folqbop4op5lO7lczIeMGWFQx2rQKwf7yWKICaPunoNeFE07o0whwrT494g3Vs6hD_Gyol16qN-YXgpet9zv-q9H1SjGjAhVLk0lToy2KXkK5BfhKWhsuh9RQXjdNUxbbHk05AoauJSUCOTeZvwDCbAAuGR3d_SYM8d\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:40%\" alt=\"“Hello Glance” Tile sample with Glance\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEinOIEmuVkJHM4htJKvBcFh4folqbop4op5lO7lczIeMGWFQx2rQKwf7yWKICaPunoNeFE07o0whwrT494g3Vs6hD_Gyol16qN-YXgpet9zv-q9H1SjGjAhVLk0lToy2KXkK5BfhKWhsuh9RQXjdNUxbbHk05AoauJSUCOTeZvwDCbAAuGR3d_SYM8d\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n            <p id=\"imgCaption\">“Hello Glance” Tile sample with Glance</p>\n           </center> <br> <p><em>Note: Using Glance-wear-tiles requires</em><code>`minSdkVersion`</code><em>&gt;= 26.</em></p> <br> <br> <h3>How it works</h3> <p> Glance creates “glanceable” experiences across Android surfaces using a base-set of <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/runtime/Composable\">Composables</a>. For Tiles on Wear OS, Glance translates Composables into <a href=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://developer.android.com/training/wearables/tiles&amp;sa=D&amp;source=docs&amp;ust=1642500000114473&amp;usg=AOvVaw3e88_9f7jPwxReN1p_fca7\">Tiles</a>. </p> <br> \n               <center> \n                <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhru4NzjUX9GD2uzLisav7EanQjrlW3-KdzivYeCXNmV0IHFXWw8xh3ycn2__bOTG_BB4hPjYTIuaBLVXeBHHCDyhm0eKI7z0nJJkjSWe9_8xoN52fBZSRUNgMKYyIQzu-XMh7nKeBSiOzvRwINstawf3LkX7Ac_BIOC6Xa2VF4vlbQr31Ym_r4vLYm\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Diagram: Glance structure\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhru4NzjUX9GD2uzLisav7EanQjrlW3-KdzivYeCXNmV0IHFXWw8xh3ycn2__bOTG_BB4hPjYTIuaBLVXeBHHCDyhm0eKI7z0nJJkjSWe9_8xoN52fBZSRUNgMKYyIQzu-XMh7nKeBSiOzvRwINstawf3LkX7Ac_BIOC6Xa2VF4vlbQr31Ym_r4vLYm\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>&nbsp;\n                <p id=\"imgCaption\">Diagram: Glance structure</p>\n               </center> <br> <p> Glance requires <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/interop/adding#anchor\">Compose to be enabled</a> and depends on Runtime, Graphics, and Unit UI <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/layering\">Compose layers</a>, but <strong>it’s not directly interoperable</strong> with other existing Jetpack Compose UI elements, like <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/wearables/compose\">Compose for Wear OS</a>. </p> <h3>What’s in the Alpha</h3> <p> This initial release introduces the main APIs to build wear Tiles: </p> \n                <ul> \n                 <li><strong><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/wear/tiles/GlanceTileService\">GlanceTileService</a></code></strong> - A service to create your tile in the composable <strong><code>Content()</code></strong> function. <li>Initial set of Glance Composables: <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#box\">Box</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#row\">Row</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#column\">Column</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/text/package-summary#text\">Text</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#image\">Image</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#spacer\">Spacer</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/wear/tiles/curved/package-summary#curvedrow\">CurvedRow</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/wear/tiles/curved/CurvedRowScope#curvedtext\">CurvedText</a></code>. <li><strong><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/GlanceModifier.html\">GlanceModifier</a></code></strong> - Plays the same role as <code>androidx.compose.ui.Modifier</code> but for the Glance composables. <li><strong><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/action/package-summary#actionstartactivity\">actionStartActivity</a></code></strong> - Starts an Activity from a user interaction. <li><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/wear/tiles/TimelineMode.SingleEntry\">TimelineMode.SingleEntry</a></code> and <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/wear/tiles/TimelineMode.TimeBoundEntries\">TimelineMode.TimeBoundEntries</a></code> - Handle single-entry and time bound timeline entries. <li><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/state/GlanceStateDefinition.html\">GlanceStateDefinition</a></code> - Persistent tile state <li><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/wear/tiles/package-summary#localtimeinterval\">LocalTimeInterval</a></code> - Local compositions (similar to <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#localstate\">LocalState</a></code>) </li> </li></li></li></li></li></li>\n                </ul> <p> We are working on bringing even more functionality with default theming, further Android Studio support, and more. Stay tuned for <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/glance\">new releases</a>. </p> <h3>Get started with Glance</h3> <p> For a quick start, take a look at the <a href=\"https://cs.android.com/androidx/platform/frameworks/support/+/androidx-main:glance/glance-wear-tiles/integration-tests/demos/src/main/java/androidx/glance/wear/tiles/demos/\">samples in the AndroidX repository</a>. Glance works with the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio\">latest stable Android Studio</a>, although since Glance relies on Compose Runtime, follow the steps on the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/interop/adding#setup\">Jetpack Compose docs</a> to set it up first. </p> <p> The Alpha version is your opportunity to influence the APIs, so please share <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=1097239&amp;template=1611667\">your feedback </a>and let us know your experience! </p> <p> Happy Composing with Glance! </p>\n <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ppvi\">Jose Alcérreca</a>, Android Developer Relations Engineer</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEijqPilH8ZItDxsIE5xhn5FozKBwNZGPnfzcvdJmumZp0fI8UmN0aKMqCHNHjopTW3uqUlroMP3IFV9LrUoQ2aqXbgpDaqkrjqoQJEuBE6Smt88Q5nz-NgAlGWXjq8eXz0ERxVtfrrx7v6MhNoL1OV43oCVgHPSfmrSu4_YWAIUKzwz8k59ErcCplII\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Blue illustration with Android phone\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/ https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEijqPilH8ZItDxsIE5xhn5FozKBwNZGPnfzcvdJmumZp0fI8UmN0aKMqCHNHjopTW3uqUlroMP3IFV9LrUoQ2aqXbgpDaqkrjqoQJEuBE6Smt88Q5nz-NgAlGWXjq8eXz0ERxVtfrrx7v6MhNoL1OV43oCVgHPSfmrSu4_YWAIUKzwz8k59ErcCplII\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>&nbsp;\n    </center> <p> As apps increase in functionality and complexity, manually testing them to verify behavior becomes tedious, expensive, or impossible. Modern apps, even simple ones, require you to verify an ever-growing list of test points such as UI flows, localization, or database migrations. Having a QA team whose job is to manually verify that the app works is an option, but fixing bugs at that stage is expensive. The sooner you fix a problem in the development process the better. </p> <p> Automating tests is the best approach to catching bugs early. Automated testing (from now on, <em>testing</em>) is a broad domain and Android offers many tools and libraries that can overlap. For this reason, beginners often find testing challenging. </p> <p> In response to this feedback, and to accommodate for Compose and new architecture guidelines, we revamped two testing sections on <a href=\"https://d.android.com\">d.android.com</a>: </p> <h2>Training</h2> <p> Firstly, there is the new <strong><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/testing\">Testing training</a></strong>, which includes the fundamentals of testing in Android with two new articles: <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/testing/fundamentals/what-to-test\">What to test</a>, an opinionated guide for beginners, and a detailed guide on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/testing/fundamentals/test-doubles\">Test doubles</a>. </p> \n    <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiWOemUDpatCmMa1JiwWWP3NCc3w5SIFV1-IocrL8kWb2II0YCa40Qy2hECirxpg76Q3fPeZ3WNycAK-KZJsefj6Sp77hvo_Rv4rU4s5nlVc-lAAAOg5YZxlcVbvr9Az512gMZKNPf2cfEyfyySRNDPGDI4N0d49Z5AXt5ivVRMrA3KvnomY7CORwZn\" style=\"display: block; This section includes an introduction to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/testing/instrumented-tests/ui-tests\">UI tests</a> and the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/testing/instrumented-tests/androidx-test-libraries/test-setup\">AndroidX Test libraries</a>. \n       <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n        <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjZSF5fsPjJqTU_3FnK1MlgAswaVi_abQ4w9kb9qRs4Z3QmKDiT2VTdf4lNspufU6E3RlzkfWMxgBkQgPTlVJCo_Z5o1f0PZcwxZGgkDuJlllCBFxpjmlVjRzBxBPQXOunDNj-Hy340U4Ri3tG9lWHlBKQC8DN4rI0YEdupdnVeTGCXZ-Dtt7AXpU2z\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:50%\" alt=\"Faking dependencies in UI tests\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1365\" data-original-width=\"1999\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjZSF5fsPjJqTU_3FnK1MlgAswaVi_abQ4w9kb9qRs4Z3QmKDiT2VTdf4lNspufU6E3RlzkfWMxgBkQgPTlVJCo_Z5o1f0PZcwxZGgkDuJlllCBFxpjmlVjRzBxBPQXOunDNj-Hy340U4Ri3tG9lWHlBKQC8DN4rI0YEdupdnVeTGCXZ-Dtt7AXpU2z\" /></a>\n       </div><p id=\"imgCaption\">Faking dependencies in UI tests</p> <h2>Tools Documentation</h2> <p> Secondly, we updated the <strong><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/test\">Testing section of the Tools documentation</a></strong> that focuses on all the tools that help you create and run tests, from <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/test/test-in-android-studio\">Android Studio</a> to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/test/command-line\">testing from the command line</a>. </p> \n       <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n        <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEglY1tp9_6lYQcY7IsMZd1KpOA1TQ7R_3lQ0YoIPqvKIPsQhd2RRJygpwB8RAl6b52CxqwV5YFcoCEPatnKkJWcuPJBFZgqRCJM8rKhEr_naqs7pX93MBfN6jIZO_w62APq-KSGK64S30KjAwYk1keASt0TgsZ65-Bm0oq-NjBcoz3DXInGboaMnPyV\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"The Unified Gradle test runner.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"958\" data-original-width=\"1999\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEglY1tp9_6lYQcY7IsMZd1KpOA1TQ7R_3lQ0YoIPqvKIPsQhd2RRJygpwB8RAl6b52CxqwV5YFcoCEPatnKkJWcuPJBFZgqRCJM8rKhEr_naqs7pX93MBfN6jIZO_w62APq-KSGK64S30KjAwYk1keASt0TgsZ65-Bm0oq-NjBcoz3DXInGboaMnPyV\" /></a>\n        <p id=\"imgCaption\">The Unified Gradle test runner.</p>\n       </div> <p> We included an article that describes <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/test/advanced-test-setup\">Advanced test setup</a> features such as working with different variants, the instrumentation manifest options, or the Android Gradle Plugin settings. </p> <p> These two new sections should give you a general notion of how and where to test your Android app. To learn more about testing specific features and libraries, you should check out their respective documentation pages. For example: <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/kotlin/flow/test\">Testing Kotlin flows</a>, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/navigation/navigation-testing\">Test Navigation</a>, or the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/training/dependency-injection/hilt-testing\">Hilt testing guide</a>. </p> <p> Sadly, machines can't automatically verify the correctness of our documentation, so if you find errors or have suggestions, please file a bug on our <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=192697&amp;template=845603&amp;pli=1\">documentation issue tracker</a>. </p>\n       <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n        <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=R3A-3W_MDRk:7xl18cBzn0Q:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"The first developer preview of Android 13 ","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/first-preview-android-13.html","description":"<meta content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiZNU5mt1NIj5H3GcopW5FzxIGv7EwrTR7hxRn7amRM4A9CexjaVK2W4GrC36JtSAOdPRsM1C6PomTtmPAjSQrAUc-jczOF_wEuTi-6UDH8D8uVcAAr9JYQwSpVNlBRRpn8T_NxhHzNqES0nGw9PWHPQUe1hW7WMQRlSS6og2zCUbpaV3fm_tT7o45B\" name=\"twitter:image\" /> \n<img src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiZNU5mt1NIj5H3GcopW5FzxIGv7EwrTR7hxRn7amRM4A9CexjaVK2W4GrC36JtSAOdPRsM1C6PomTtmPAjSQrAUc-jczOF_wEuTi-6UDH8D8uVcAAr9JYQwSpVNlBRRpn8T_NxhHzNqES0nGw9PWHPQUe1hW7WMQRlSS6og2zCUbpaV3fm_tT7o45B\" style=\"display: none;\" /> \n<p><em>Posted by Dave Burke, VP of Engineering</em></p>\n<p> </p>\n<p><img alt=\"Android13 Logo\" height=\"300\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjnrShXcFkBmErmhgdmx82vJbaKBIxU6p2Yz2Vr1V7AlFkD2tGwRmx_a7tWcInPmiUh8VpPmEEqXut-EjP23lFYG9wiMO4sKBDEwbZ3MNppZOy_HW54OXO4SkdQVH08cWdi7QnTMMwGELFoPq_r7_cyaGU8fx2InJG2R-NfkqF1IRt7rKOfA8M1GhUy\" style=\"float: right; margin-bottom: 0.3px; margin-right: 10px;\" width=\"300px\" /></p> \n<p> Every day, billions of people around the world pull out their Android device to help them get things done. That Android works well for each and every one of them is ensured in part through a collaborative process with you, our developer community, sharing feedback to help us make Android stronger. </p> \n<p> Today, we’re sharing a first look at the next release of Android, with the Android 13 Developer Preview 1. With Android 13 we’re continuing some important themes: privacy and security, as well as developer productivity. We’ll also build on some of the newer <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/10/12L-preview-large-screens.html\">updates we made in 12L</a> to help you take advantage of the 250+ million large screen Android devices currently running. </p> \n<p> This is just the start for Android 13, and we’ll have lots more to share as we move through the release. Read on for a taste of what’s new, and visit the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13\">Android 13 developer site</a> for details on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/download\">downloads for Pixel</a> and the release <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/overview#timeline\">timeline</a>. As always, it’s crucial to get your feedback early, to help us include it in the final release. We’re looking forward to hearing what you think, and thanks in advance for your continued help in making Android a platform that works for everyone! </p> \n<br /> \n<h2>Privacy &amp; security at the core</h2> \n<p> People want an OS and apps that they can trust with their most personal and sensitive information. Privacy is core to Android’s product principles, and Android 13 focuses on building a responsible and high quality platform for all by providing a safer environment on the device and more controls to the user. In today’s release, we’re introducing a photo picker that allows users to share photos and videos securely with apps, and a new Wi-Fi permission to further minimize the need for apps to have the location permission. We recommend trying out the new APIs and testing how the changes may affect your app. </p> \n<p> <strong>Photo picker and APIs</strong> - To help protect photo and video privacy of users, Android 13 adds a system photo picker — a standard and optimized way for users to share both local and cloud-based photos securely. Android’s long standing document picker allows a user to share specific documents of any type with an app, without that app needing permission to view all media files on the device. The photo picker extends this capability with a dedicated experience for picking photos and videos. Apps can use the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/features/photopicker\">photo picker APIs</a> to access the shared photos and videos without needing permission to view all media files on the device. We plan to bring the photo picker experience to more Android users through Google Play system updates, as part of a MediaProvider module update for devices (excepting Go devices) running Android 11 and higher. Give photo picker APIs a try and <a href=\"https://android.devsite.corp.google.com/about/versions/13/feedback\">let us know your feedback</a>! </p> \n<br> \n <center> \n  <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhDnB4kN5X9g6wZ7pl6xAvzDNbHgEdQsMeCSS2bjcYr05DE-8pGzcMlX0aqaQnOCSnhi3gCXrhpaxhGdsaRcGX_y6QsSBBFcnbhl_smp0ogy-IQCGJs0mPQrMRmLAOwUBcn0QmudLXqHCboLZgM9OmZgJaiKB6nyRg3Mgo5nGti8frzf5vRxV92Cl1z\"><img alt=\"Photo picker provides a consistent, secure way for users to give apps access to specific photos and videos.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"714\" data-original-width=\"1058\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhDnB4kN5X9g6wZ7pl6xAvzDNbHgEdQsMeCSS2bjcYr05DE-8pGzcMlX0aqaQnOCSnhi3gCXrhpaxhGdsaRcGX_y6QsSBBFcnbhl_smp0ogy-IQCGJs0mPQrMRmLAOwUBcn0QmudLXqHCboLZgM9OmZgJaiKB6nyRg3Mgo5nGti8frzf5vRxV92Cl1z\" style=\"width: 35%;\" /></a> \n  <p id=\"imgCaption\" style=\"line-height:1em; padding-top:1em;\">Photo picker provides a consistent, secure way for users <br>to give apps access to specific photos and videos.</br></p>\n </center> <br> <p> <strong>Nearby device permission for Wi-Fi - </strong>Android 13 introduces the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/Manifest.permission.html#NEARBY_WIFI_DEVICES\">NEARBY_WIFI_DEVICES</a> runtime permission (part of the NEARBY_DEVICES permission group) for apps that manage a device's connections to nearby access points over Wi-Fi. The new permission will be required for apps that call <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/features/nearby-wifi-devices-permission#check-for-apis-that-require-permission\">many commonly-used Wi-Fi APIs</a>, and enables apps to discover and connect to nearby devices over Wi-Fi without needing location permission. Previously, the location permission requirements were a challenge for apps that needed to connect to nearby Wi-Fi devices but didn’t actually need the device location. Apps targeting Android 13 will be now able to request the NEARBY_WIFI_DEVICES permission with the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/R.attr.html#usesPermissionFlags\">“neverForLocation” flag </a>instead, which should help promote a privacy-friendly app design while reducing friction for developers. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/features/nearby-wifi-devices-permission\">Learn more</a>. </p> <br /> <h2>Developer productivity and tools</h2> <p> Android 13 also brings new features and tools for developer productivity. Helping you create beautiful apps that run on billions of devices is one of our core missions – whether it’s in Android 13 or through our tools for <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/modern-android-development\">modern Android development</a>, like a language you love in Kotlin or opinionated APIs with Jetpack. By helping you work more productively, we aim to lower your cost of development so you can focus on continuing to build amazing experiences. Here’s some of what’s new in today’s release. </p> <p> <strong>Quick Settings Placement API</strong> - Quick Settings in the notification shade is a convenient way for users to change settings or take quick actions without leaving the context of an app. For apps that provide <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/service/quicksettings/TileService\">custom tiles</a>, we’re making it easier for users to discover and add your tiles to Quick Settings. Using a new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/StatusBarManager#requestAddTileService(android.content.ComponentName,%20java.lang.CharSequence,%20android.graphics.drawable.Icon,%20java.util.concurrent.Executor,%20java.util.function.Consumer%3Cjava.lang.Integer%3E)\">tile placement API</a>, your app can now prompt the user to directly add your custom tile to the set of active Quick Settings tiles. A new system dialog lets the user add the tile in one step, without leaving your app, rather than having to go to Quick Settings to add the tile. </p> <br> \n   <center> \n    <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjYJX8m9RfURIZ7Y6lonoMxAopKaI6twe7faZDk3NnJzo_5mVOg6dqKCI-CrnCMO9_h_wafBJU57r5rt0CDBnyFalQurxULEcZ3II98dp_IE5OEzfLLPGiu0Bimacd6BtaaQ-myjzWQvVNFEH6em8ziuJ7dhQGvrt8--uM2fD-wianb5hRSIBDC4rfx\"><img alt=\"Tile service sample wants to add the following tile to Quick Settings Alert\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"714\" data-original-width=\"1058\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjYJX8m9RfURIZ7Y6lonoMxAopKaI6twe7faZDk3NnJzo_5mVOg6dqKCI-CrnCMO9_h_wafBJU57r5rt0CDBnyFalQurxULEcZ3II98dp_IE5OEzfLLPGiu0Bimacd6BtaaQ-myjzWQvVNFEH6em8ziuJ7dhQGvrt8--uM2fD-wianb5hRSIBDC4rfx\" style=\"width: 50%;\" /></a>&nbsp;\n   </center> <br> <p> <strong>Themed app icons</strong> - In Android 13 we’re extending Material You dynamic color beyond Google apps to all app icons, letting users opt into icons that inherit the tint of their wallpaper and other theme preferences. All your app needs to supply is a <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/features#themed-app-icon-specs\">monochromatic app icon</a> (for example, your notification drawable) and a tweak to the adaptive icon XML. We’re encouraging all developers to provide compatible icons to help provide a consistent experience for users who have opted in. Themed app icons are initially supported on Pixel devices and we’re working with our device manufacturer partners to bring them to more devices. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/features#themed-app-icons\">Learn more</a>. </p> <br> \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEisJ4y2QVpDoB9fsvbBsIvNe_fS8cTIW6iaDY8B69lfyA85ZJnyatcdy-PCt25XqCf4DDxS8ogVbzxnftvdaNBoSdf2rPKYxl2CZF1rh3qL7yNfhz2d4rF1GcubEPSpQuhCuViW9O6m4aCloBj2YGLqXpgVKrXmmSVuOa3B1oZUysod5okHAeUs4qMh\"><img alt=\"Three phone screens. The first screen has themed icons disabled. The second has themed icons enabled. And the third has themed icons &amp; dark theme enabled\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"714\" data-original-width=\"1058\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEisJ4y2QVpDoB9fsvbBsIvNe_fS8cTIW6iaDY8B69lfyA85ZJnyatcdy-PCt25XqCf4DDxS8ogVbzxnftvdaNBoSdf2rPKYxl2CZF1rh3qL7yNfhz2d4rF1GcubEPSpQuhCuViW9O6m4aCloBj2YGLqXpgVKrXmmSVuOa3B1oZUysod5okHAeUs4qMh\" style=\"width: 100%;\" /></a>&nbsp;\n     </center> <br> <p> <strong>Per-app language preferences - </strong>Some apps let users choose a language that differs from the system language, to meet the needs of multilingual users. Such apps can now call <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/app/LocaleManager\">a new platform API</a> to set or get the user’s preferred language, helping to reduce boilerplate code and improve compatibility when setting the app’s runtime language. For broader compatibility, we'll be adding a similar API in an upcoming Jetpack library. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/features/app-languages\">Learn more</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Faster hyphenation</strong> - Hyphenation makes wrapped text easier to read and helps make your UI more adaptive. In Android 13 we’ve optimized hyphenation performance by as much as 200% so you can now enable it in your TextViews with almost no impact on rendering performance. To enable faster hyphenation, use the new <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/TextView#attr_android:hyphenationFrequency\">fullFast</a></code> or <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/TextView#attr_android:hyphenationFrequency\">normalFast</a></code> frequencies in <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/TextView#setHyphenationFrequency(int)\">setHyphenationFrequency()</a></code>. Give faster hyphenation a try and let us know what you think!</p> <strong>Programmable shaders</strong> - Android 13 adds support for programmable <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/graphics/RuntimeShader\">RuntimeShader</a> objects, with behavior defined using the Android Graphics Shading Language (AGSL). AGSL shares much of its syntax with GLSL, but works within the Android rendering engine to customize painting within Android's canvas as well as filtering of View content. Android internally uses these shaders to implement <a href=\"https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/master:frameworks/base/graphics/java/android/graphics/drawable/RippleShader.java;l=24?q=RippleShader&amp;sq=\">ripple effects</a>, <a href=\"https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/master:frameworks/native/libs/renderengine/skia/filters/BlurFilter.cpp?q=RuntimeShader&amp;ss=android%2Fplatform%2Fsuperproject&amp;start=21\">blur</a>, and <a href=\"https://cs.android.com/android/platform/superproject/+/master:frameworks/base/tests/HwAccelerationTest/src/com/android/test/hwui/StretchShaderActivity.java?q=RuntimeShader&amp;ss=android%2Fplatform%2Fsuperproject&amp;start=11\">stretch overscroll</a>, and Android 13 enables you to create similar advanced effects for your app. <br> \n       <center> \n        <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh8Kl639YB4_hQJf1ryAOkTopIG_w_Z1KzegbHLznIUv_KaLngpASPpRCwU57Non8wF0fwljar6F_S0Xg82_xkjucgA5JQ6Rw4DXkqeh3Pf4_XEKqJkOSAZ0l7j6bU5Af2kaqJk7Na1ZZbp4aiFIUz4ndzyl76LDfm6_sJSty_mfeGYjnaargtCzwhs=w200-h200\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:270px\" alt=\"AGSL animated shader\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh8Kl639YB4_hQJf1ryAOkTopIG_w_Z1KzegbHLznIUv_KaLngpASPpRCwU57Non8wF0fwljar6F_S0Xg82_xkjucgA5JQ6Rw4DXkqeh3Pf4_XEKqJkOSAZ0l7j6bU5Af2kaqJk7Na1ZZbp4aiFIUz4ndzyl76LDfm6_sJSty_mfeGYjnaargtCzwhs=w200-h200\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n        <p id=\"imgCaption\" style=\"line-height:1em; padding:1em\">AGSL animated shader, adapted<br> from <a href=\"https://twitter.com/notargs/status/1250468645030858753\">this GLSL Shader</a></br></p>\n       </center> <p> <strong>OpenJDK 11 updates</strong> - In Android 13 we’ve started the work of refreshing Android's Core Libraries to align with the OpenJDK 11 LTS release, with both library updates and Java 11 programming language support for app and platform developers. We also plan to bring these Core Library changes to more devices through Google Play system updates, as part of an ART module update for devices running Android 12 and higher. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/features#core-libraries\">Learn more</a>. </p> <br /> <h2>App compatibility</h2> <p> With each platform release we’re working to make updates faster and smoother by prioritizing app compatibility as we roll out new platform versions. In Android 13 we’ve made most app-facing changes opt-in to give you more time, and we’ve updated our tools and processes to help you get ready sooner. </p> <p> <strong>More of Android updated through Google Play </strong>- In Android 13 we’re continuing to expand our investment in <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2019/05/fresher-os-with-projects-treble-and-mainline.html\">Google Play system updates</a> (Project Mainline) to give apps a more consistent, secure environment across devices, and to deliver new features and capabilities to users. We can now push new features like photo picker and OpenJDK 11 directly to users on older versions of Android through updates to existing modules. We’ve also added new modules, such as the Bluetooth and Ultra wideband modules, to further expand the scope of Android’s updatable core functionality. </p> <p> <strong>Optimizing for tablets, foldables, and Chromebooks </strong>- With all the momentum in large screen devices like tablets, foldables, and Chromebooks, now is the time to get your apps ready for these devices and design fully adaptive apps that fit any screen. You can get started using our guidance on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/docs/quality-guidelines/tablet-app-quality\">optimizing for tablets</a>, then learn how to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/large-screens/get-started-with-large-screens\">build for large screens</a> and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/ui/foldables\">develop for foldables</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Easier testing and debugging of changes</strong> - To make it easier for you to test the opt-in changes that can affect your app, we’ll make many of them toggleable again this year. WIth the toggles you can force-enable or disable the changes individually from Developer options or <code>adb</code>. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/reference/compat-framework-changes\">Check out the details here</a>. </p> <br> \n        <center> \n         <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh8Iv9_18qTnHUzgBr6bUQcSLgUT9kIyZweK8pb5zH-OhaxHdzDjdnI049uxhFmp_YjtLMUJe3mCNKZ_NWKc-J9IlTYHxMAENSnXrTX3nf5hWB8IOrTCEs6LZv9xP0X8pMR7ffmKvJm-F4p5L5-IkMfJngSS9FK6N6g81N1r6qzm1Wd5d7MPZvj9deb\"><img alt=\"App compatibility toggles in Developer Options.\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"714\" data-original-width=\"1058\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh8Iv9_18qTnHUzgBr6bUQcSLgUT9kIyZweK8pb5zH-OhaxHdzDjdnI049uxhFmp_YjtLMUJe3mCNKZ_NWKc-J9IlTYHxMAENSnXrTX3nf5hWB8IOrTCEs6LZv9xP0X8pMR7ffmKvJm-F4p5L5-IkMfJngSS9FK6N6g81N1r6qzm1Wd5d7MPZvj9deb\" style=\"width: 50%;\" /></a>\n         <p id=\"imgCaption\">App compatibility toggles in Developer Options.</p>\n        </center> <br> <p> <strong>Platform stability milestone</strong> - Like last year, we’re letting you know our Platform Stability milestone well in advance, to give you more time to plan for app compatibility work. At this milestone we’ll deliver not only final SDK/NDK APIs, but also final internal APIs and app-facing system behaviors. This year we’re expecting to reach Platform Stability in June 2022, and from that time you’ll have several weeks before the official release to do your final testing. The release timeline details are <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/overview\">here</a>. </p> <br> \n          <center> \n           <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEheauQQSr6IkpUJiMtm3Dcnd6f49gL6SQ_B9iRb_BcKH4aXo1mTKW0pj31VccnE2na2_lmb1e6Yxhui9Vt_6cpm5XhUN3_m1mDl7grOc6zhzmsUC71LWuUgA0U4ysj5KsNjA8DXuDfYIPsZGNN0KUPHc9tI0_bV4zNv-O3ZDt9iJm01s0TiEqrxU8p0\"><img alt=\"Timeline. February and March Developer Previews. April-Final Release Beta Releases. June-Final Release Platform Stability\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"714\" data-original-width=\"1058\" id=\"imgFull\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEheauQQSr6IkpUJiMtm3Dcnd6f49gL6SQ_B9iRb_BcKH4aXo1mTKW0pj31VccnE2na2_lmb1e6Yxhui9Vt_6cpm5XhUN3_m1mDl7grOc6zhzmsUC71LWuUgA0U4ysj5KsNjA8DXuDfYIPsZGNN0KUPHc9tI0_bV4zNv-O3ZDt9iJm01s0TiEqrxU8p0\" style=\"width: 100%;\" /></a>&nbsp;\n          </center> <br> <h2>Get started with Android 13</h2> <p> The Developer Preview has everything you need to try the Android 13 features, test your apps, and give us <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/feedback\">feedback</a>. For testing your app with tablets and foldables, the easiest way to get started is using the Android Emulator in a tablet or foldable configuration - <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/12L/get\">complete setup instructions are here</a>. For phones, you can get started on a device today by <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/download\">flashing a system image</a> to a <strong>Pixel 6 Pro, Pixel 6, Pixel 5a 5G, Pixel 5, Pixel 4a (5G), Pixel 4a, Pixel 4 XL, or Pixel 4 </strong>device. If you don’t have a Pixel device, you can use the 64-bit system images with the Android Emulator in Android Studio. For even broader testing, GSI images are available. </p> <p> When you’re <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/setup-sdk\">set up</a>, here are some of the things you should do: </p> \n           <ul> \n            <li><strong>Try the new features and APIs</strong> - your feedback is critical during the early part of the developer preview. Report issues in our tracker or give us direct feedback by survey for selected features from the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/feedback\">feedback and requests</a> page. </li>\n            <li><strong>Test your current app for compatibility</strong> - learn whether your app is affected by default behavior changes in Android 13. Just install your current published app onto a device or emulator running Android 13 and test. </li>\n            <li><strong>Test your app with opt-in changes</strong> - Android 13 has opt-in behavior changes that only affect your app when it’s targeting the new platform. It’s extremely important to understand and assess these changes early. To make it easier to test, you can <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/reference/compat-framework-changes\">toggle the changes on and off individually</a>. </li> \n           </ul> <p> We’ll update the preview system images and SDK regularly throughout the Android 13 release cycle. This initial preview release is <strong>for developers only</strong> and not intended for daily or consumer use, so we're making it available by <strong>manual download only</strong>. Once you’ve manually installed a preview build, you’ll automatically get future updates over-the-air for all later previews and Betas. <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13/get\">More here</a>. </p> <p> As we reach our Beta releases, we'll be inviting consumers to try Android 13 as well, and we'll open up enrollments for the Android Beta program at that time. For now, please note that Android Beta is not yet available for Android 13. </p> <p> For complete information, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/13\">visit the Android 13 developer site</a>. </p> <p> <em>Java and OpenJDK are trademarks or registered trademarks of Oracle and/or its affiliates.</em> </p><p></p><p></p>\n           <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n Last month, we <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/jetpack-compose-11-now-stable.html\">released version 1.1 of Jetpack Compose</a>, which contains new features like improved focus handling, touch target sizing, ImageVector caching, and support for Android 12 stretch overscroll. Compose 1.1 also graduates a number of previously experimental APIs to stable and supports newer versions of Kotlin. In #TheAndroidShow, we’ll take you behind-the-scenes in the world of animations with one of the engineers who helps build them, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/doris4lt?lang=en\">Doris Liu</a>. And then we hear from Twitter about how Compose helps them build new features in half the time! </p> <br> <h2><strong>Next: the world of tablets, including the 12L feature drop, now in AOSP</strong></h2> <p> Next up, we’ll jump into the world of tablets, following the big news from earlier this week: we’ve officially released the 12L feature drop to AOSP and it’s rolling out to all supported Pixel devices over the next few weeks. There are over 250+ million large screen Android devices, and 12L makes Android 12 even better on tablets, and includes updates like a new taskbar that lets users instantly drag and drop apps into split-screen mode, new large-screen layouts in the notification shade and lockscreen, and improved compatibility modes for apps. You can <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/android/12l-larger-screens/\">read more here</a>. </p> <p> Starting later this year, 12L will be available in planned updates on tablets and foldables from Samsung, Lenovo and Microsoft, so now is the time to make sure your apps are ready. We highly recommend testing your apps in split-screen mode with windows of various sizes, trying it in different orientations, and checking the new compatibility mode changes if they apply. You can read more about 12L for developers <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/12L\">here</a>. </p> <p> We see large screens as a key surface for the future of Android, and we’re continuing to invest to give you the tools you need to build great experiences for tablets, Chromebooks, and foldables. You can learn more about how to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/large-screens/get-started-with-large-screens\">get started optimizing for large screens</a>, and make sure to check out our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/large-screens\">large screens developer resources</a>. </p> <br> <h2>Tune in now! </h2> <p> Finally, we wrap up the show with a conversation with the director for Android Developer Relations, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mabouza\">Maru Ahues Bouza</a>, where we talk about Android 13 as well as some of the broader themes you’ll continue to see from
