src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiLpPXqzAHXPX0dNtI4ef0_A97d1ZdOtuDhT4kCef5MMcLT5G6KuAwVMTHJQPIMu9uY4J-8smQ7k-sC_Tq460B_3S5yq4pHom1JWolJ46mNHoes_2SPhpTuZj_i9-3BgNFkO1YMBxtfUd3MFZOUH_Y80JbKkYD6LYz-gNjyWXvsH_NY3-k2WCfIHwUZ\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n    </center> <p> Last year, mobile game consumer spending grew <a href=\"https://www.gamesindustry.biz/articles/2022-01-20-newzoo-mobile-game-revenue-generated-usd93bn-in-2021\">7.3%</a> to <a href=\"https://www.gamesindustry.biz/articles/2022-01-20-newzoo-mobile-game-revenue-generated-usd93bn-in-2021\">$93.2</a> billion with no signs of slowing down. In this competitive, growing market, effectively monetizing your audience has never been more important. But without access to a strategy consultant, how can you know if your monetization strategy is as strong as it can be? </p> <p> That’s why we’re expanding the suite of tools available in Play Console to help it be exactly that. Last year, we released new <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/03/google-play-console-powers-better.html\">engagement and monetization metrics</a> on the Statistics page to help you grow your business, and now we’re pleased to announce <strong>new strategic guidance tools to help you drive successful monetization</strong>. </p> <p> In this new section, you’ll see our metric-driven guidance to help you better monetize your game by: </p> \n    <ol> \n     <li><strong>Contextualizing your topline revenue:</strong> Understand how your game’s revenue metrics contribute to your overall business goals, and learn when to prioritize optimizing for one metric over another. <li><strong>Identifying opportunities: </strong>Find out where there is an opportunity to improve a metric by benchmarking against peer groups, and explore insights by country. <li><strong>Recommending next steps:</strong> Learn how to take advantage of monetization opportunities with specific actions you can take right away. </li> </li></li>\n    </ol> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh55JpUqSIVriLdSvsciWDbdhx4vBrnQ8NV319Qz1fqgZbhKIZ0SGVZYETnDv15H62r-3Rer8XI1u9JhnFzd9t8MxHVHc4_elRqbngVBKOkAVz5PNhoYePGFpsbWJ5dw--H420qYCQBo88cS0ypmhMzbV-paN_iWdmeG4UnjHH9WktZwPg_9L4IuqCv\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"screenshot of strategic guidance for monetization webpage in Google Play Console\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEh55JpUqSIVriLdSvsciWDbdhx4vBrnQ8NV319Qz1fqgZbhKIZ0SGVZYETnDv15H62r-3Rer8XI1u9JhnFzd9t8MxHVHc4_elRqbngVBKOkAVz5PNhoYePGFpsbWJ5dw--H420qYCQBo88cS0ypmhMzbV-paN_iWdmeG4UnjHH9WktZwPg_9L4IuqCv\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n     <p id=\"imgCaption\">The strategic guidance metric hierarchy. (<a href=\"https://medium.com/googleplaydev/a-kpis-guide-for-google-play-apps-and-games-intro-to-metrics-214da979f5a2\">Learn more</a> or visit our Play Academy for specific courses like <a href=\"https://playacademy.exceedlms.com/student/path/36716/activity/61566\"> monitoring KPIs.</a>)</p>\n    </center> <p> We’ve spent the last couple of years perfecting our guidance, and testing the dashboard with selected partners. Feedback on our strategic guidance has been positive — and we hope you’ll find it useful, too. </p> \n    <center>\n     <p><em>“This is extremely useful! These type of insights are actually what we expect from Google, because this is something that really can help us to scale our business.” </em></p> \n     <p><em>- Product Manager at Gameloft</em></p>\n    </center> <br> <h3>Understand key monetization drivers and their relationships with the metric hierarchy</h3> <p> <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/u/0/developers/app/strategic-guidance/monetization/overview\">Strategic guidance</a> can be found in Financial reports within Play Console. In partnership with experts in mobile games growth, we’ve included primary monetization metrics (including new metrics) and their relationships to help you easily assess your performance and measure against your peers. You can see all the metrics in this <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/11452323\">Help Center article</a>. </p> <p> The metric hierarchy is a tool to help you understand how you and your teams can directly influence the lower-level metrics of your games performance, like buyer conversions, which contribute to your overall top-line business performance.<strong> Using peerset comparisons and per-country breakdowns, you can quickly identify your biggest growth opportunities: what markets are underperforming and where you are a market leader. </strong> </p> <br> <h3>Explore metric analysis to turn insights into action</h3> <p> Select a metric and explore it in detail to track your performance over time. Strategic guidance shows you a breakdown of your chosen metric by location to help you spot opportunities to expand your game globally. The detailed metric analysis also helps you identify where a small investment has an outsized return. </p> \n      <center> \n       <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjANLb3Rsij8jBvEde4rcMAkxq1KFqsefyFEaVX5-oqYw5fx0eqzV33fOn6ocauldxb2u5nbGh_IJvJ-9x2FF1CEaS5GzEVdcw7ITjD-ByL4gyGixfwQux-PeAhsr18YlYSqVbbVdTeCB1_Z-DKzT9dLdcRjXCTTDnYNCQ1w3r0D2xo9LuMeQMi70fh\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Strategic guidance metric recommendation example for returning daily buyer ratio.\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjANLb3Rsij8jBvEde4rcMAkxq1KFqsefyFEaVX5-oqYw5fx0eqzV33fOn6ocauldxb2u5nbGh_IJvJ-9x2FF1CEaS5GzEVdcw7ITjD-ByL4gyGixfwQux-PeAhsr18YlYSqVbbVdTeCB1_Z-DKzT9dLdcRjXCTTDnYNCQ1w3r0D2xo9LuMeQMi70fh\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n       <p id=\"imgCaption\">Strategic guidance metric recommendation example for returning daily buyer ratio.</p>\n      </center> <p> Whether you’ve created a casual game or an RPG, the metric-specific recommendations are designed to be insightful and relevant to a variety of game developers. They can be used to help you diversify your promotional content, refine your game mechanics, or test new price points that enable purchasing power parity. </p> <br> <h3>Get IAP monetization guidance today, with more insights to come </h3> <p> With an increasing number of developers shifting focus from an ads-only monetization business model to include in-app purchases (IAP), we’ve developed strategic guidance to be most relevant for developers that include IAP-monetization as part of their overall strategy. With this launch, we’re excited to bring growth consulting opportunities to these game developers at scale. Stay tuned for more launches this year to help you successfully drive your revenue growth. </p> \n       <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n        <a 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Announcing Jetpack Glance Alpha for app widgets","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/12/announcing-jetpack-glance-alpha-for-app.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgol-A5cMCZY79MH5v0axcekWIVJ--ymPUe0U5Q4BLsC0BA1LTbWIlZ76XWi2cHjxHVu-kbpv0o2QJWBjNAda_93Ah7AW_PcAgz9o082cd6zyTJZAM8HjQnrZ69A6CaKQaCFuf2LLi4p6xRvS_WUn9tVA2K2wmV3_qB6JDKnFNhO3Guvn5tPc_SuoaY\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgol-A5cMCZY79MH5v0axcekWIVJ--ymPUe0U5Q4BLsC0BA1LTbWIlZ76XWi2cHjxHVu-kbpv0o2QJWBjNAda_93Ah7AW_PcAgz9o082cd6zyTJZAM8HjQnrZ69A6CaKQaCFuf2LLi4p6xRvS_WUn9tVA2K2wmV3_qB6JDKnFNhO3Guvn5tPc_SuoaY\"> <p><em>Posted by Marcel Pintó Biescas, Developer Relations Engineer,<a href=\"https://twitter.com/marxallski\"> @marxallski</a></em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgol-A5cMCZY79MH5v0axcekWIVJ--ymPUe0U5Q4BLsC0BA1LTbWIlZ76XWi2cHjxHVu-kbpv0o2QJWBjNAda_93Ah7AW_PcAgz9o082cd6zyTJZAM8HjQnrZ69A6CaKQaCFuf2LLi4p6xRvS_WUn9tVA2K2wmV3_qB6JDKnFNhO3Guvn5tPc_SuoaY\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Illustration of a laptop with the Android rocket logo\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgol-A5cMCZY79MH5v0axcekWIVJ--ymPUe0U5Q4BLsC0BA1LTbWIlZ76XWi2cHjxHVu-kbpv0o2QJWBjNAda_93Ah7AW_PcAgz9o082cd6zyTJZAM8HjQnrZ69A6CaKQaCFuf2LLi4p6xRvS_WUn9tVA2K2wmV3_qB6JDKnFNhO3Guvn5tPc_SuoaY\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n    </center> <p> Android 12 <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/features/widgets\">revamps</a> a key feature for many Android users, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/appwidgets/overview\">App Widgets</a>, making them more useful, beautiful, and discoverable (84% use at least 1 widget). Today, we’re making it even easier to build them by releasing the first alpha of <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/glance\">Jetpack Glance</a>, a new framework built on top of the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/compose-runtime\">Jetpack Compose runtime</a> designed to make it faster and easier to build app widgets for the home screen and other surfaces. </p> <p> We’d love you to give it a try and <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=1097239&amp;template=1611667\">share your feedback</a>! </p> <p> Glance offers similar modern, declarative Kotlin APIs that you are used to with <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a>, helping you build beautiful, responsive app widgets with way less code. <br> </br></p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhCxQ1FBHq-7cO30VysSZuz0EzVCxy_HEDj2_pVwPiSK_8qvItf0nSNrKUFIdU8nCeITffEpdpT90CMFc2tJXPRJufmVQxGLLeFa9nZf5FM2Sq-1jf9gm_XtB1xzdcTOgQ0rMBTBruaZh4f7r_qEp5_8W7pXWNcbvy2f_LVPJI1IjtlToTy9SBWcaNN\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"Glance “Hello World” widget sample\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhCxQ1FBHq-7cO30VysSZuz0EzVCxy_HEDj2_pVwPiSK_8qvItf0nSNrKUFIdU8nCeITffEpdpT90CMFc2tJXPRJufmVQxGLLeFa9nZf5FM2Sq-1jf9gm_XtB1xzdcTOgQ0rMBTBruaZh4f7r_qEp5_8W7pXWNcbvy2f_LVPJI1IjtlToTy9SBWcaNN\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\">Glance “Hello World” widget sample</p>\n    </center> <br> <td> <pre class=\"prettyprint\">class GreetingsWidget(private val name: String): GlanceAppWidget() {\n    @Composable\n    override fun Content() {\n        Text(text = \"Hello $name\")\n    }\n}\n\nclass GreetingsWidgetReceiver : GlanceAppWidgetReceiver() {\n\n    override val glanceAppWidget = GreetingsWidget(\"Glance\")\n}\n</pre> </td> <h2>How it works</h2> <p> Glance provides a base-set of Composables to help build “glanceable” experiences. Starting today with app widget components but with more coming. Using the Jetpack Compose runtime, Glance can translate <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/runtime/Composable\">Composables</a> into actual <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/RemoteViews\">RemoteViews</a>, and display them in an app widget.</p> <br> \n      <center> \n       <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEggMg_RzkopYSTx7ASIFIIENF-IIawryxoOo-HwCvY2c_3T2wTUtQpSowT2UxcW3RQgDmBER9sJHGDHrDpDz9KdgXwLy6RM-i02MKoLya_Td9YkQKh1Dz5XE5vbkZbohzepgQPh-azszWtQI9Ky1p_8asnEZ0ZEETBOJBID9-52ytwA5UT5OGZoKE__\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"Diagram: Glance structure\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEggMg_RzkopYSTx7ASIFIIENF-IIawryxoOo-HwCvY2c_3T2wTUtQpSowT2UxcW3RQgDmBER9sJHGDHrDpDz9KdgXwLy6RM-i02MKoLya_Td9YkQKh1Dz5XE5vbkZbohzepgQPh-azszWtQI9Ky1p_8asnEZ0ZEETBOJBID9-52ytwA5UT5OGZoKE__\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n       <p id=\"imgCaption\">Diagram: Glance structure</p>\n      </center> <br> <p> This means that Glance requires <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/interop/adding#anchor\">Compose to be enabled</a> and depends on Runtime, Graphics, and Unit UI <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/layering\">Compose layers</a>, but <strong>it’s not directly interoperable</strong> with other existing Jetpack Compose UI elements. However, state or any other logic within your app can be shared to create a glanceable UI. </p> <br> <h2>What's in Alpha</h2> <p> This initial release introduces the main APIs to enable you to build app widgets in addition to providing interoperability with existing RemoteViews. </p> <p> Here’s an overview of what the library offers, at a glance: </p> \n        <ul> \n         <li>Declare your app widgets with <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/GlanceAppWidget\">GlanceAppWidget</a></code> and <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/GlanceAppWidgetReceiver\">GlanceAppWidgetReceiver</a></code>. <li>Compose your UI with the initial set of Glance Composables: <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#box\">Box</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#row\">Row</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#column\">Column</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/text/package-summary#text\">Text</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#button\">Button</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/lazy/package-summary#lazycolumn\">LazyColumn</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#image\">Image</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/layout/package-summary#spacer\">Spacer</a></code>. <li>Apply modifiers to the composables using <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/GlanceModifier.html\">GlanceModifier</a></code> methods. <li>Handle user interaction with predefined <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/action/package-summary\">Action</a></code>s. \n             <ul> \n              <li><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/action/package-summary#actionstartactivity\">actionStartActivity</a></code> <li><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/action/package-summary#actionruncallback\">actionRunCallback</a></code> <li><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/action/package-summary#actionstartservice\">actionStartService</a></code> <li><code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/action/package-summary#actionstartbroadcastreceiver\">actionStartBroadcastReceiver</a></code> </li></li></li></li>\n             </ul> <li>Provide parameters to <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/action/package-summary\">Action</a></code> with <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/action/ActionParameters\">ActionParameters</a></code>. <li>Handle <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/guide/topics/appwidgets/layouts\">different size modes</a> by defining <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/SizeMode.Single\">SizeMode.Single</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/SizeMode.Exact\">SizeMode.Exact</a></code> or <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/SizeMode.Responsive\">SizeMode.Responsive</a></code>. <li>Persist <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/state/package-summary\">GlanceAppWidget state</a></code> by providing a <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/state/GlanceStateDefinition.html\">GlanceStateDefinition</a></code>. <li>Local compositions like <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#localcontext\">LocalContext</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#localstate\">LocalState</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#localglanceid\">LocalGlanceId</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/package-summary#localsize\">LocalSize</a></code>. <li>Interop with your existing <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/widget/RemoteViews.html\">RemoteViews</a></code> with the <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/glance/appwidget/package-summary#androidremoteviews\">AndroidRemoteViews</a></code> Composable. </li> </li></li></li></li></li></li></li></li>\n        </ul> <p> We are working on bringing even more functionality with default theming, further Android Studio support, and more. Stay tuned for <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/glance\">new releases</a>. </p> <br> <p><em>Note: while the minSDK is 21, we are currently only supporting compatibility till SDK v23.</em></p> <iframe width=\"100%\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/15Q7xqxBGG0\" title=\"YouTube video player\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> <br> <h2>Get started with Glance</h2> <p> Check out <a href=\"https://github.com/android/user-interface-samples/tree/glance/AppWidget/glance-widget\">the sample</a> on GitHub for a quick start. Glance works with the latest <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio\">stable Android Studio</a>, although since Glance relies on Compose Runtime, follow the steps on <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/interop/adding#setup\">the Jetpack Compose docs</a> to set it up first. </p> <p> In addition, for a more advanced showcase, checkout <a href=\"https://cs.android.com/androidx/platform/frameworks/support/+/androidx-main:glance/glance-appwidget/integration-tests/demos/src/main/java/androidx/glance/appwidget/demos/\">the demos in the AndroidX repository</a>. </p> <br> \n           <center> \n            <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhynsyDKiaahKLF-tCajggeTyXBdCVTlqQ7VZZJWSGNmpxtg-zGhUc-hSfhBjgP0it74HM-MsaFxKHqR6ePiKbbX2UlV4_tDw25qvKcDpH-c5MhlGBX0a8IRLhjS1YqrrSBQG3ib-0K_a3EllT00hAeRXu8zFX9YaLypTygpxkud9Cb--HfpYBWbMVV\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"ResponsiveAppWidget.kt demo\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhynsyDKiaahKLF-tCajggeTyXBdCVTlqQ7VZZJWSGNmpxtg-zGhUc-hSfhBjgP0it74HM-MsaFxKHqR6ePiKbbX2UlV4_tDw25qvKcDpH-c5MhlGBX0a8IRLhjS1YqrrSBQG3ib-0K_a3EllT00hAeRXu8zFX9YaLypTygpxkud9Cb--HfpYBWbMVV\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n            <p id=\"imgCaption\"><a demo</p>\n           </center> <p> The Alpha version is your opportunity to influence the APIs, so please share <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=1097239&amp;template=1611667\">your feedback </a>and let us know your experience! </p> <p> Happy Composing with Glance! </p> \n 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Play Time with Jetpack Compose","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/03/play-time-with-jetpack-compose.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEi6y_NUo9gnpHYdRc7lwnbVnraBtUSIZTnIoAcHXkbq8Z0AFHBUHDI_s7HwwP2h2nTwo571RnRuXN-sUWdgJ7qkNb2MSslYiXWP3tteXooTdwAS_YzbZMTux25eLZk0kgdLtXmWTRLdolft-ZcsgGjCyJnH-CjzHsZXGy8vNVxB5oFZkBExOpBwvoDL\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEi6y_NUo9gnpHYdRc7lwnbVnraBtUSIZTnIoAcHXkbq8Z0AFHBUHDI_s7HwwP2h2nTwo571RnRuXN-sUWdgJ7qkNb2MSslYiXWP3tteXooTdwAS_YzbZMTux25eLZk0kgdLtXmWTRLdolft-ZcsgGjCyJnH-CjzHsZXGy8vNVxB5oFZkBExOpBwvoDL\"> <h3><em>Learn about Google Play Store’s strategy for adopting Jetpack Compose, how they overcame specific performance challenges, and improved developer productivity and happiness.</em></h3> <p><em>Posted by Andrew Flynn &amp; Jon Boekenoogen, Tech leads on Google Play</em><p> <p> In 2020, Google Play Store engineering leadership made the big decision to revamp its entire storefront tech stack. The existing code was 10+ years old and had incurred tremendous tech debt over countless Android platform releases and feature updates. We needed new frameworks that would scale to the <strong>hundreds of engineers</strong> working on the product while not negatively impacting <strong>developer productivity</strong>, <strong>user experience, or the performance</strong> of the store itself. </p> <p> We laid out a multi-year roadmap to update everything in the store from the network layer all the way to the pixel rendering. As part of this we also wanted to adopt a modern, declarative UI framework that would satisfy our product goals around interactivity and user delight. After analyzing the landscape of options, we made the bold (at the time) decision to commit to <strong><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a></strong>, which was still in pre-Alpha. </p> <p> Since that time, the Google Play Store and Jetpack Compose teams at Google have worked extremely closely together to release and polish a version of Jetpack Compose that meets our specific needs. In this article we'll cover our approach to migration as well as the challenges and benefits we found along the way, to share some insight into what adopting Compose can be like for an app with many contributors. </p> \n    <center>\n     <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEi6y_NUo9gnpHYdRc7lwnbVnraBtUSIZTnIoAcHXkbq8Z0AFHBUHDI_s7HwwP2h2nTwo571RnRuXN-sUWdgJ7qkNb2MSslYiXWP3tteXooTdwAS_YzbZMTux25eLZk0kgdLtXmWTRLdolft-ZcsgGjCyJnH-CjzHsZXGy8vNVxB5oFZkBExOpBwvoDL\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img alt=\"Play Store rewrote their UI with 50% less code with Compose\" style=\"width:100%\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1080\" data-original-width=\"1920\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEi6y_NUo9gnpHYdRc7lwnbVnraBtUSIZTnIoAcHXkbq8Z0AFHBUHDI_s7HwwP2h2nTwo571RnRuXN-sUWdgJ7qkNb2MSslYiXWP3tteXooTdwAS_YzbZMTux25eLZk0kgdLtXmWTRLdolft-ZcsgGjCyJnH-CjzHsZXGy8vNVxB5oFZkBExOpBwvoDL\" /></a>\n     </div>\n    </center> <br> <h2>Considerations</h2> <p> When we were considering Jetpack Compose for our new UI rendering layer, our top two priorities were: </p> \n     <ol> \n      <li><strong>Developer Productivity:</strong> Play Store team has hundreds of engineers contributing to this code, so it should be easy (and fun) to develop against. <li><strong>Performance:</strong> Play Store renders lots of media-heavy content with many business metrics that are very sensitive to latency and jank, so we needed to make sure it performed well across <strong>all</strong> devices, especially low-memory hardware and Android (Go Edition) devices. </li> </li>\n     </ol> <br> <h3>Developer Productivity</h3> <p> We have been writing UI code using Jetpack Compose for <strong>over a year now</strong> and enjoy how Jetpack Compose makes UI development more simple. </p> <p> We love that <strong>writing UI requires much less code, sometimes up to 50%</strong>. This is made possible by Compose being a declarative UI framework and harnessing Kotlin’s conciseness. Custom drawing and layouts are now simple function calls instead of View subclasses with N method overrides. </p> <p> Using the Ratings Table as an example: </p> \n      <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n       <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgcmmVZ5wincH-Pje9YIe0WHfb0ZBOWl4xNt5IbIPNteb7iFyvw9KtiXIjz6mQ3V9VKh9tm-K8lPQgNQmZNl8Po7WloN7Ks-mqYWp2Mr906Vm3Z13y9RBLhWdLqch6JCVmslK6ISSNEg_kqGYcmV-pclO_YtpnfHeAa6t7pM17uDgTQB3zgo1t0SzYV\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"ratings table\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"189\" data-original-width=\"618\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgcmmVZ5wincH-Pje9YIe0WHfb0ZBOWl4xNt5IbIPNteb7iFyvw9KtiXIjz6mQ3V9VKh9tm-K8lPQgNQmZNl8Po7WloN7Ks-mqYWp2Mr906Vm3Z13y9RBLhWdLqch6JCVmslK6ISSNEg_kqGYcmV-pclO_YtpnfHeAa6t7pM17uDgTQB3zgo1t0SzYV\" /></a>\n      </div> <p> With Views, this table consists of: </p> \n      <ul> \n       <li>3 View classes total, with 2 requiring custom drawing for the rounded rects, and stars <li>~350 lines of Java, 55 lines of XML </li> </li>\n      </ul> <p> With Compose, this table consists of: </p> \n      <ul> \n       <li>All <code>@Composable</code> functions contained in the same file and language! <li>~210 lines of Kotlin </li> </li>\n      </ul> <p> </p><p><img alt=\"buffering GIF\" height=\"220\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEj9dVqrcKRGBY0Q4CfyQFq5vJRNIZPNV8PtGj3X3fd_qDx6eJS0JHR2iRRva4_uhIsFgzB3OkWL7YK5lQ3J5_wTPd1vfURkYC_3Y5TtQREgsXG7rQJ57NK1x7Di63lHGWofzA0pS0rZJfUPtFtZSiIsTBS7iabYRRL7LcKfigsyKQOseRd65VmzbCRm\" style=\"float: right; margin-bottom: 0.3px; margin-right: 10px;\" width=\"220px\" /></p> <strong>Animations</strong> are a <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z_T1bVjhMLk\">hailed feature of Compose</a> for their simplicity and expressiveness. Our team is building motion features that delight our Play Store users more than ever with Compose. With Compose’s declarative nature and animations APIs, <strong>writing sequential or parallel animations has never been easier</strong>. Our team no longer fears all the corner cases of animations around cancellation and call back chaining. <a href=\"https://airbnb.io/projects/lottie-android/\">Lottie</a>, a popular animation library, already provides Compose APIs that are simple to work with. <p> Now you might be thinking: this all sounds great, but what about library dependencies that provide Views? It's true, not all library owners have implemented Compose-based APIs, especially when we first migrated. However, Compose provides <strong>easy View interoperability</strong> with its <code>ComposeView</code> and <code>AndroidView</code> APIs. We successfully integrated with popular libraries like <a href=\"https://exoplayer.dev/\">ExoPlayer</a> and <a href=\"https://developers.google.com/youtube/android/player\">YouTube’s Player</a> in this fashion. </p> \n      <center>\n       <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n        <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjwtSLBwzAjtel5VQweS_uj3BvOk1Y2A7LeFV0dgpGJ8erCG8t0YKCloeUY9Y9NhcNRD0LGnWCfmBydncD1AYacw2uvL2-mwvO7z9ArRdhpDyPkg7Z7RmNw8T-0YfhzVqFobFKzCMaCpGvt0fN89GtC6xVhr3OGF1Q2s16NFrcwGnURK4mVgWg6S_0P\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Headshot of Andrew\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1081\" data-original-width=\"1921\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjwtSLBwzAjtel5VQweS_uj3BvOk1Y2A7LeFV0dgpGJ8erCG8t0YKCloeUY9Y9NhcNRD0LGnWCfmBydncD1AYacw2uvL2-mwvO7z9ArRdhpDyPkg7Z7RmNw8T-0YfhzVqFobFKzCMaCpGvt0fN89GtC6xVhr3OGF1Q2s16NFrcwGnURK4mVgWg6S_0P\" /></a>\n       </div>\n      </center> <br> <h3>Performance</h3> <p> The Play Store and Jetpack Compose teams worked closely together to make sure Compose could run as fast and be as jank-free as the View framework. Due to how Compose is bundled within the app (rather than being included as part of the Android framework), this was a tall order. Rendering individual UI components on the screen was fast, but end to end times of loading the entire Compose framework into memory for apps was expensive. </p> <p> One of the largest Compose adoption performance improvements for the Play Store came from the development of <strong><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/studio/profile/baselineprofiles\">Baseline Profiles</a></strong>. While <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2019/04/improving-app-performance-with-art.html\">cloud profiles</a> help improve app startup time and have been available for some time now, they are only available for API 28+ and are not as effective for apps with frequent (weekly) release cadences. To combat this, the Play Store and Android teams worked together on Baseline Profiles: a developer-defined, bundled profile that app owners can specify. They ship with your app, are fully compatible with cloud profiles and can be defined both at the app-level of specificity and library-level (Compose adopters will get this for free!). By rolling out baseline profiles, Play Store saw a <strong>decrease in initial page rendering time</strong> on its search results page <strong>of 40%</strong>. That’s huge! </p> <p> <strong>Re-using UI components</strong> is a <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/lifecycle\">core mechanic</a> of what makes Compose performant for rendering, particularly in scrolling situations. Compose does its best to skip recomposition for composables that it knows can be skipped (e.g. they are immutable), but developers can also force composables to be treated as skippable if all parameters meet the <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/runtime/Stable\">@Stable</a></code> annotation requirements. The Compose compiler also provides a <a href=\"https://github.com/androidx/androidx/blob/androidx-main/compose/compiler/design/compiler-metrics.md\">handy guide</a> on what is preventing specific functions from being skippable. While creating heavily re-used UI components in Play Store that were used frequently in scrolling situations, we found that unnecessary recompositions were adding up to missed frame times and thus jank. We built a <code><a href=\"https://github.com/android/snippets/blob/master/compose/recomposehighlighter/src/main/java/com/example/android/compose/recomposehighlighter/RecomposeHighlighter.kt\">Modifier</a></code> to easily spot these recompositions in our debug settings as well. By applying these techniques to our UI components, <strong>we were able to reduce jank by 10-15%.</strong></p> \n       <center> \n        <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjrA4HErEi7ovyWGTl4iClAzJCT6JHEJkB7-x4bCCd9TFAr6C3BCS7fstZ2CX3Wcs3EBF9yLDDPPoIm_2DrIKKe5BgUpYjfGc-OxTif0KNa-nhspBgntOnNBqg9iHUF8IsP5bXLPOVw8ZarsGQ6xW3nZ35esbcdiIocKlQBWo1_eFv5VGGJGTzi6PXn\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"Recomposition visualization Modifier in action\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEjrA4HErEi7ovyWGTl4iClAzJCT6JHEJkB7-x4bCCd9TFAr6C3BCS7fstZ2CX3Wcs3EBF9yLDDPPoIm_2DrIKKe5BgUpYjfGc-OxTif0KNa-nhspBgntOnNBqg9iHUF8IsP5bXLPOVw8ZarsGQ6xW3nZ35esbcdiIocKlQBWo1_eFv5VGGJGTzi6PXn\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n        <p id=\"imgCaption\" style=\"line-height:1em; padding:1em\">Recomposition visualization Modifier in action. Blue (no recompositions), Green (1 recomposition).</p>\n       </center> <p> Another key component to optimizing Compose for the Play Store app was having a detailed, <strong>end-to-end migration strategy for the entire app</strong>. During initial integration experiments, we ran into the Two Stack Problem: running both Compose and View rendering within a single user session was very memory intensive, especially on lower-end devices. This cropped up both during rollouts of the code on the same page, but also when two different pages (for example, the Play Store home page and the search results page) were each on a different stack. In order to ameliorate this startup latency, it was important for us to have a concrete plan for the <strong>order and timeline of pages migrating to Compose</strong>. Additionally, we found it helpful to add short-term pre-warming of common classes as stop-gaps until the app is fully migrated over. </p> <p> Compose unbundling from the Android framework has reduced the overhead in our team directly contributing to Jetpack Compose, resulting in fast turnaround times for improvements that benefit all developers. We were able to collaborate with the Jetpack Compose team and launch features like <a href=\"https://r.android.com/1789196\">LazyList item type caching</a> as well as move quickly on lightweight fixes like <a href=\"https://r.android.com/1950996\">extra object allocations</a>. </p> \n       <center>\n        <div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both;\">\n         <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhSjbt-KVkwZrpwDu1KnM-CGfcTrhc4I-mdqONbOQ9V4Nmx6PzfoBIH_hN2qLeav9bedAYFaca3jRm40xD9yg_rLDANu5sCHypD-3vDplL8p001xqExCkAbyA7_dmm5DFZBJ9vCcmMAFCSaNDJcSdPx9x6-g2lsNExULF9JPNh6MJt1ye-29eD8XRO7\" style=\"display: block; padding: 1em 0; text-align: center; \"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Headshot of Jon\" border=\"0\" data-original-height=\"1081\" data-original-width=\"1921\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhSjbt-KVkwZrpwDu1KnM-CGfcTrhc4I-mdqONbOQ9V4Nmx6PzfoBIH_hN2qLeav9bedAYFaca3jRm40xD9yg_rLDANu5sCHypD-3vDplL8p001xqExCkAbyA7_dmm5DFZBJ9vCcmMAFCSaNDJcSdPx9x6-g2lsNExULF9JPNh6MJt1ye-29eD8XRO7\" /></a>\n        </div>\n       </center> <br> <h2>Looking Ahead</h2> <p> The Play Store’s adoption of Compose has been a boon for our team’s developer happiness, and <strong>a big step-up for code quality and health</strong>. All new Play Store features are built on top of this framework, and Compose has been instrumental in unlocking <strong>better velocity and smoother landings for the app</strong>. Due to the nature of our Compose migration strategy, we haven’t been able to measure things like <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose/ergonomics#apk-and-build\">APK size</a> changes or build speed as closely, but all signs that we can see look very positive! </p> <p> <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/compose\">Compose</a> is the future of Android UI development, and from the Play Store’s point of view, we couldn’t be happier about that! </p> \n        <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n         <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=Y_l7Je-JcCU:t4rI2LdNqWM:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n         <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?a=Y_l7Je-JcCU:t4rI2LdNqWM:-BTjWOF_DHI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?i=Y_l7Je-JcCU:t4rI2LdNqWM:-BTjWOF_DHI\" yreaderx/cdn88@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-26-49-604_6c69e2fb75ece36e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn7@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-26-47-709_e6aa4d73b74f71ed.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/blogspot/hsDu?i=Y_l7Je-JcCU:t4rI2LdNqWM:-BTjWOF_DHI":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647246393391},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Keeping Google Play safe with our key 2022 initiatives","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/03/privacy-and-security-direction.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhh3FMLL-etD7iDzhSI6CoYbuwgB9ZADjXa6A9C4aM3W-eRqj1FGfP8dyMY4i5RlMtQJD8Sx1y1NHFuaCae10iZkAs_cETaCAllzCDU075awpkAc1pkhld7uxwjTmwNdihGhB-FtySiSsf9aknd1ZULz0zkRtybX4gRUp8JCbPh2n3pPEhjK0mTjNWS\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhh3FMLL-etD7iDzhSI6CoYbuwgB9ZADjXa6A9C4aM3W-eRqj1FGfP8dyMY4i5RlMtQJD8Sx1y1NHFuaCae10iZkAs_cETaCAllzCDU075awpkAc1pkhld7uxwjTmwNdihGhB-FtySiSsf9aknd1ZULz0zkRtybX4gRUp8JCbPh2n3pPEhjK0mTjNWS\"> <p><em>Posted by Krish Vitaldevara Director, Product Management, Play and Android Trust &amp; Safety</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhh3FMLL-etD7iDzhSI6CoYbuwgB9ZADjXa6A9C4aM3W-eRqj1FGfP8dyMY4i5RlMtQJD8Sx1y1NHFuaCae10iZkAs_cETaCAllzCDU075awpkAc1pkhld7uxwjTmwNdihGhB-FtySiSsf9aknd1ZULz0zkRtybX4gRUp8JCbPh2n3pPEhjK0mTjNWS\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Safety illustration\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhh3FMLL-etD7iDzhSI6CoYbuwgB9ZADjXa6A9C4aM3W-eRqj1FGfP8dyMY4i5RlMtQJD8Sx1y1NHFuaCae10iZkAs_cETaCAllzCDU075awpkAc1pkhld7uxwjTmwNdihGhB-FtySiSsf9aknd1ZULz0zkRtybX4gRUp8JCbPh2n3pPEhjK0mTjNWS\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>&nbsp;\n    </center> <p> Keeping Google Play safe for users and developers remains our top priority. Over the past year, we’ve partnered with developers to ensure their apps are safe. We helped developers to <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/google/play/integrity\">protect their apps</a>, prepare to share their <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/10/launching-data-safety-in-play-console.html\">data safety practices</a> with users, and collaborate on <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/android/introducing-privacy-sandbox-android/\">building more private advertising technology</a>. We also continued investing in machine-learning detection and enhanced app review processes to <a href=\"https://security.googleblog.com/2021/04/how-we-fought-bad-apps-and-developers.html\">stop apps with abusive or malicious content</a> before anyone can install them. </p> <p> We also realize that it can be challenging for developers to keep up with the pace of change in this evolving privacy and security landscape. We’ve been mindful to give developers clearer updates, more time for substantial changes, and more helpful information through Inbox Console Messages, global webinars, and additional education resources. Today, we’re excited to share more about what’s ahead in 2022 to give you plenty of time to prepare. </p> <h2>What we look forward to this year</h2> <p> <strong>Giving everyone a clear way to understand an app’s data safety practices</strong> </p> <p> Developers want to explain data safety to users in a clear and simple way. In the <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/10/launching-data-safety-in-play-console.html\">upcoming</a> <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/10787469\">Data safety section</a> in your app’s Play store listing, you can share how your app collects, shares, and protects user data. Users told us that they value having this information to help them decide if an app is right for them. They’ll start to see the Data safety section in Google Play store in late April, so make sure to submit your <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/developers/app/app-content/summary\">Data safety form</a> soon. Completed Data Safety forms will be required for all app updates starting July 20. </p> <p> <strong>Building a more privacy-friendly approach to advertising </strong> </p> <p> We recently <a href=\"https://blog.google/products/android/introducing-privacy-sandbox-android/\">announced</a> that we’re expanding the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/design-for-safety\">Privacy Sandbox</a> initiative to Android. We’re working on innovative solutions to improve user privacy, while continuing to support key mechanisms that developers rely on to build their businesses and provide access to free apps for everyone. We’re building this technology in close collaboration with developers. Join our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/design-for-safety/ads/subscribe\">email newsletter</a> to stay updated. </p> <p> <strong>Protecting developers' apps from privacy and fraudulent activity</strong> </p> <p> Last <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TyxL78e5Bag\">fall</a>, we started rolling out the new <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/google/play/integrity\">Play Integrity API</a> to help you protect their games and apps and ensure that users have the intended experience that you designed. Now, everyone has access to this new API, making it easier to detect suspicious traffic and respond faster to issues like fraud and cheating. We've built this in a future-forward way so that you can easily get new features with little build time required to upgrade. Learn how to set it up for your apps <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/google/play/integrity/overview\">here</a>. </p> <p> <strong>Helping developers navigate SDKs</strong> </p> <p> Developers shared that they want faster communication from SDK providers about critical updates, so last year we gave SDK providers a way to <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/10358880\">notify you about urgent issues</a> in your Google Play Console. You’ve also shared that you want to learn more about an SDK’s safety and reliability to avoid wasting build time or exposing users to unsafe practices. In a few months, we’ll start sharing information like an SDK’s adoption levels, its retention rate, and the runtime permission it uses to help you choose the right SDK for your business and users. </p> <p> <strong>Enhancing protections for kids and families</strong> </p> <p> <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/07/announcing-policy-updates-to-bolster.html\">Last year</a>, we continued to refine our <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/9876714#new-090121\">advertising restrictions</a> and <a href=\"https://support.google.com/googleplay/android-developer/answer/9876714#new_04012022\">parental control</a> requirements to further enhance privacy and safety for kids. Eligible developers can now add a badge to their upcoming Data safety section, highlighting that they’re committed to following our <a href=\"https://play.google.com/console/about/families/\">Families policy</a>. You’ll also see continued policy updates this year designed to help protect kids' safety and privacy. Join our policy webinars or watch our <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLWz5rJ2EKKc_vmK_ZwtyM08GzUxKltSTp\">PolicyBytes</a> to stay updated. </p> <p> <strong>Responsible Data Collection and Use</strong> </p> <p> Developers should only collect and use the data required for app functionality and improvement. For practical tips on this front, you can view our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/design-for-safety#privacy\">best practices</a> guide. This year, we’re continuing to align permissions more closely with the appropriate use cases. We’re also in active conversations with developers about ways to mitigate risks from apps that leverage APIs in older Android OS versions. Stay tuned to our policy update emails, as we’ll share more soon. </p> <p> Thank you for your partnership in making Google Play a safe and trustworthy platform for everyone. </p>\n    <div <p><em>Posted by The Android Team</em><p> <p> Google Chrome is the most widely used browser globally, and the Chrome team wants to ensure their users have a great experience across all devices. Many Chrome users have been requesting more productivity features on their mobile, tablet, and foldable devices to better match the capabilities of Chrome on desktop. To meet these needs, the team decided to invest in building features that encourage multitasking capabilities. While the team built this for phones as well, they wanted to especially focus on implementing these features where people would use them the most: large screen devices such as tablets and foldables. </p> <br> \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEigetrVSFyU5Hf7JRwLygWSt--xxWQBELffzfxLqNjR5_yq899maqeHPmcF0sce6Fu7eqbFBNe66ettQ6SaOhyMBQpYtaRfyZKrJZ2aYlrJlSGrR1uivSF9Mp57pAT9jmZRLhmQ_AGiTmEwfKzWsKw0gcckf0GAJLolTIpstDf2_9x8Nd0nySMZh3C5\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"GIF showing multitasking on a tablet with multiple instances\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEigetrVSFyU5Hf7JRwLygWSt--xxWQBELffzfxLqNjR5_yq899maqeHPmcF0sce6Fu7eqbFBNe66ettQ6SaOhyMBQpYtaRfyZKrJZ2aYlrJlSGrR1uivSF9Mp57pAT9jmZRLhmQ_AGiTmEwfKzWsKw0gcckf0GAJLolTIpstDf2_9x8Nd0nySMZh3C5\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n     </center> <br> <h2>What they did</h2> <p> The team first decided to focus on building a way for people to open multiple Chrome windows (instances) side by side. They took advantage of <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/about/versions/12/12L/summary#multitasking\">12L features</a> such as the taskbar and also took advantage of the Samsung edge panel. </p> <p> They utilized the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/R.attr#launchMode\">singleInstancePerTask</a> launch mode to build the side-by-side functionality. They wanted to balance allowing people to use many windows at once with making sure the feature was still usable. The team researched usability best practices, observed other multi-window experiences on large screen devices, and thought through limitations to ensure optimal device memory usage. They determined people could comfortably use up to five windows side by side on large screen devices, and the team updated their app to support this functionality. </p> <p> The team wanted to make it easier for their users to take advantage of this feature, so they added a “New Window” shortcut in the menu. They used the new capability of intent flag combo <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/android/content/Intent#FLAG_ACTIVITY_LAUNCH_ADJACENT\">LAUNCH_ADJACENT|NEW_TASK</a> to create this shortcut. Having this feature be more prominently displayed in the product greatly improved the usage. They saw<strong> multi-window usage improve by 18x. </strong> </p> <br> <h2>Results</h2> <p> This is a new feature, and the Chrome team has already seen that <strong>multi-instance for the Chrome app is used 42% more on tablets and foldables</strong> than on phones that support the feature. This usage demonstrates the functionality resonated well with Chrome users on large screen devices, and that it was worth investing in building these features to enhance the experience for Chrome users on large screens. </p> <p> They also had very positive feedback from their large screen users in the form of app reviews. “<em>This app is fabulous 👌! You can split screen, change tabs, and much more. You can also play a lot of games in it. I prefer to five star this app</em>.” </p> <p> The team has future plans to further improve the Chrome experience on large screens to help their users be more productive. </p> <br> \n        <center> href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhUKnPETjkInnB8UVG_oPWaOCz5-MMAl1v7Efmz1wv9hSf_f35pZPbux2EPrd4pe6Qoi8FrCYfrPR0j2zA3vK4M0gT3QjQ-fKp7OAJI9yyLcGEdcstQohy5VsBVnBE34yK_C396B8ErFBDa2FgFl1ansEILiRc4KusktM6lCC_OR3NU_oHCJqLYvfPs\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n        </center> <br> <h2>Get started </h2> <p> Learn more about how you can get started with optimizing your app for <a 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Rebuilding our guide to app architecture","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/12/rebuilding-our-guide-to-app-architecture.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgnJ0CCtKClhEOE_BDOoWiXGr2eA6LWjn-RPvFjFx8Va97f_1_xCmpF3uI_bUILoQPqJUDlXUbIRVPjvi3oCiFtRVZlcAAkHBa1cJlufG5OvmeovQeiHgH9bLhxREufi-fw7FnxIcmxGmzWuW0DmYUZolsM6rywTSZIm3KtI6yx9jSIeRpuYzRZubke\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgnJ0CCtKClhEOE_BDOoWiXGr2eA6LWjn-RPvFjFx8Va97f_1_xCmpF3uI_bUILoQPqJUDlXUbIRVPjvi3oCiFtRVZlcAAkHBa1cJlufG5OvmeovQeiHgH9bLhxREufi-fw7FnxIcmxGmzWuW0DmYUZolsM6rywTSZIm3KtI6yx9jSIeRpuYzRZubke\"> <p><em>Posted by Manuel Vicente Vivo, Developer Relations Engineer, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/manuelvicnt\"> @manuelvicnt</a></em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgnJ0CCtKClhEOE_BDOoWiXGr2eA6LWjn-RPvFjFx8Va97f_1_xCmpF3uI_bUILoQPqJUDlXUbIRVPjvi3oCiFtRVZlcAAkHBa1cJlufG5OvmeovQeiHgH9bLhxREufi-fw7FnxIcmxGmzWuW0DmYUZolsM6rywTSZIm3KtI6yx9jSIeRpuYzRZubke\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Android robot under a flow chart graphic\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgnJ0CCtKClhEOE_BDOoWiXGr2eA6LWjn-RPvFjFx8Va97f_1_xCmpF3uI_bUILoQPqJUDlXUbIRVPjvi3oCiFtRVZlcAAkHBa1cJlufG5OvmeovQeiHgH9bLhxREufi-fw7FnxIcmxGmzWuW0DmYUZolsM6rywTSZIm3KtI6yx9jSIeRpuYzRZubke\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <br> <p> As Android apps grow in size, it's important to design the code with an architecture in place to allow the app to <strong>scale</strong>, improve <strong>quality</strong> and <strong>robustness</strong>, and make it <strong>easier to test</strong>. </p> <p> An app architecture defines the <strong>boundaries</strong> between parts of the app and the <strong>responsibilities</strong> each part should have. This favors the <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_concerns\">separation of concerns</a> principle that enables the aforementioned benefits. </p> <p> In response to community demand for up-to-date guidance on app architecture, <strong>we're launching a <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide\">revamped guide to app architecture</a></strong>. This includes best practices and recommended architecture for building robust, high-quality apps. It also provides a page for each layer of the recommended architecture: <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide/ui-layer\">UI</a>, <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide/domain-layer\">domain</a>, and <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide/data-layer\">data</a> layers. Within them, you'll find deep dives into more complex topics, such as how to handle <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide/ui-layer/events\">UI events</a>. </p> <p> Each Android app should have at least two layers: </p> \n     <ul> \n      <li>The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide/ui-layer\">UI layer</a> that displays application data on the screen. <li>The <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide/data-layer\">data layer</a> that contains the business logic of your app and exposes application data. </li> </li>\n     </ul> <p> You can add an additional layer called the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/guide/domain-layer\">domain layer</a> to simplify and reuse the interactions between the UI and data layers. </p> \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEi9J4PtTryeHRes2oL_uqldpBfebky8BTG9JnfwGD1dzIeh-6CLaOvGqVgJuzC9FXPW6TfhB7LppVMMJqA7scDnECSojcbh8qi8ja8jhrxouYCdC5AOlFiU7ykHkqKY1MU1GUNJdjkOyjYKCtWvX3YZTljGE-G_a3E1rdYCl8wnb7CbVSKP4J_NbjHV\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"flow chart showing UI layer, domain layer, data layer\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEi9J4PtTryeHRes2oL_uqldpBfebky8BTG9JnfwGD1dzIeh-6CLaOvGqVgJuzC9FXPW6TfhB7LppVMMJqA7scDnECSojcbh8qi8ja8jhrxouYCdC5AOlFiU7ykHkqKY1MU1GUNJdjkOyjYKCtWvX3YZTljGE-G_a3E1rdYCl8wnb7CbVSKP4J_NbjHV\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n      <p id=\"imgCaption\">General diagram of a typical app architecture. The UI layer gets the application data from the optional domain layer, or the data layer, that exposes application data.</p>\n     </center> <br> <p> We have created a <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/courses/pathways/android-architecture\">learning pathway</a> to help you consume this content in order and in a trackable way. Don't miss the chance to learn all of this and get a badge as recognition! </p> <br> \n       <center> \n        <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgAqH8sIWG17lOXp1rwyp5S5vxpXDhP0j4rPfOrODeE7bWbOhZ2FISbyqY4-oYJxaAUvEr-sNalLZAn2hLi4NNH2UIFhSnrpJb1TIn-aow9W_PVravlfD5rJxDMixEKqUKSUxDErXSxAbIGey-QFrBVw9Nx1UElfLTbp8rzHyiePpvVUSC6c_1VVuTx\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:75%\" alt=\"badge\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/12/ https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgAqH8sIWG17lOXp1rwyp5S5vxpXDhP0j4rPfOrODeE7bWbOhZ2FISbyqY4-oYJxaAUvEr-sNalLZAn2hLi4NNH2UIFhSnrpJb1TIn-aow9W_PVravlfD5rJxDMixEKqUKSUxDErXSxAbIGey-QFrBVw9Nx1UElfLTbp8rzHyiePpvVUSC6c_1VVuTx\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n       </center> <h2>Is this for you?</h2> <p> If you’re a <strong>beginner</strong>, you should begin by <strong>understanding the benefits</strong> of having an app architecture and then follow these recommendations as a first approach to the topic. <strong>Intermediate and advanced</strong> developers can <strong>follow</strong> these recommendations and <strong>customize</strong> them to their needs. In fact, our research suggests that most professional developers are already using these best practices. </p> <p> You might be wondering if you should update your existing architecture to follow this recommendation, and the answer is no… or wait… it's up to you. If your current architecture works for your team, you might want to stick with it. But you might also find patterns in our guides you can benefit from and incorporate into your app. </p> <h2>We’re not done yet</h2> <p> This is the first batch of documents we're releasing, with more to come in 2022. Help us make the guidance better! If you have any feedback on the current recommendations or if you want to see other architecture-related topics in them, let us know in our <a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=192697&amp;template=845603\">docs issue tracker</a>. </p>\n       <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n        <a 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Jetpack Compose 1.1 is now stable!","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/jetpack-compose-11-now-stable.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiEIiQOoFF-f-sDcbYOMINZw5-2R9aQjrREfiXFMGsRYODVfaz1sgdCS2C3UjgeJjCII5oyE4y97kbvQIUsl9wIx8RqTSZPSdIoCywW89lvmAJ5a15bkFOwoR9UacCEUb4CjOMy0omVMfC0CQhUfz9VMTZR4iyjDGagEZfNuMid8BT0lvarns9Tp6PC\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiEIiQOoFF-f-sDcbYOMINZw5-2R9aQjrREfiXFMGsRYODVfaz1sgdCS2C3UjgeJjCII5oyE4y97kbvQIUsl9wIx8RqTSZPSdIoCywW89lvmAJ5a15bkFOwoR9UacCEUb4CjOMy0omVMfC0CQhUfz9VMTZR4iyjDGagEZfNuMid8BT0lvarns9Tp6PC\"> <p><em>Posted by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/fmuntenescu\">Florina Muntenescu</a>, Android Developer Relations Engineer</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiEIiQOoFF-f-sDcbYOMINZw5-2R9aQjrREfiXFMGsRYODVfaz1sgdCS2C3UjgeJjCII5oyE4y97kbvQIUsl9wIx8RqTSZPSdIoCywW89lvmAJ5a15bkFOwoR9UacCEUb4CjOMy0omVMfC0CQhUfz9VMTZR4iyjDGagEZfNuMid8BT0lvarns9Tp6PC\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Blue background with phone icon\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEiEIiQOoFF-f-sDcbYOMINZw5-2R9aQjrREfiXFMGsRYODVfaz1sgdCS2C3UjgeJjCII5oyE4y97kbvQIUsl9wIx8RqTSZPSdIoCywW89lvmAJ5a15bkFOwoR9UacCEUb4CjOMy0omVMfC0CQhUfz9VMTZR4iyjDGagEZfNuMid8BT0lvarns9Tp6PC\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a> \n    </center> <p> Today, we’re releasing version 1.1 of <a href=\"https://d.android.com/compose\">Jetpack Compose</a>, Android's modern, native UI toolkit, continuing to build out our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/compose-roadmap\">roadmap</a>. This release contains new features like improved focus handling, touch target sizing, <code>ImageVector</code> caching, and support for Android 12 stretch overscroll. Compose 1.1 also graduates a number of previously experimental APIs to stable and supports newer versions of Kotlin. We've already updated our <a href=\"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/goo.gle/compose-samples\">samples</a>, <a href=\"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/goo.gle/compose-pathway\">codelabs,</a> and <a href=\"https://github.com/google/accompanist\">Accompanist library</a> to work with Compose 1.1. </p> <h2>New stable features and APIs</h2> <h3>Image vector caching</h3> <p> Compose 1.1 introduces image vector caching bringing big performance improvements. We’ve added a caching mechanism to <code>painterResource</code> API to cache all instances of <code>ImageVector</code>s that are parsed with a given resource id and theme. The cache will be invalidated on configuration changes. </p> <h3>Touch target sizing</h3> <p> With respect to Compose 1.0, Material components will expand their layout space to meet Material <a href=\"https://material.io/design/usability/accessibility.html\">accessibility guidelines</a> <a href=\"https://material.io/design/usability/accessibility.html#layout-and-typography\">touch target size</a>. For instance, a <code>RadioButton's</code> touch target will expand to a minimum size of 48x48dp, even if you set the <code>RadioButton</code>'s size to be smaller. This aligns Compose Material to the same behavior of Material Design Components, providing consistent behavior if you mix Views and Compose. This change also ensures that when you create your UI using Compose Material components, minimum requirements for touch target accessibility will be met. </p> <p> If you find this change breaks existing layout logic, set <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/material3/package-summary#LocalMinimumTouchTargetEnforcement()\">LocalMinimumTouchTargetEnforcement</a></code> to <code>false </code>to disable this behavior, but please be mindful this might reduce the usability of your app, and should be used with caution. </p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgX-RUgE9W2qlxlA1JOk3hXlDesekuVA-BO12Ceu51EDx7bvZrjDo_PMcrmvuLKYmbGkHUUBQk8rcK1F98FIWTqxwLAKlWAkgVWr9QT5icJCIGXnIGEzA-iR1M-5gXouJr1mBCdjHokavZ-ydFJIYGs7kl468No_ruLEcywEMvE9Xuku5mSUlJjDu0f\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"RadioButton touch target update \nLeft: Compose 1.0, right: Compose 1.1 \n\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEgX-RUgE9W2qlxlA1JOk3hXlDesekuVA-BO12Ceu51EDx7bvZrjDo_PMcrmvuLKYmbGkHUUBQk8rcK1F98FIWTqxwLAKlWAkgVWr9QT5icJCIGXnIGEzA-iR1M-5gXouJr1mBCdjHokavZ-ydFJIYGs7kl468No_ruLEcywEMvE9Xuku5mSUlJjDu0f\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>&nbsp; \n     <p id=\"imgCaption\">RadioButton touch target update<br> Left: Compose 1.0, right: Compose 1.1 </br></p> \n    </center> <h2>Experimental to stable APIs</h2> <p> Several APIs graduated from experimental to stable. Highlights include: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li>Animation related APIs, such as: <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/animation/EnterTransition\">EnterTransition</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/animation/ExitTransition\">ExitTransition</a></code>, some of the <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/animation/package-summary#AnimatedVisibility(kotlin.Boolean,androidx.compose.ui.Modifier,androidx.compose.animation.EnterTransition,androidx.compose.animation.ExitTransition,kotlin.String,kotlin.Function1)\">AnimatedVisibility</a></code> APIs, <li>Vector related APIs: <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/ui/graphics/vector/package-summary#rememberVectorPainter(androidx.compose.ui.unit.Dp,androidx.compose.ui.unit.Dp,kotlin.Float,kotlin.Float,kotlin.String,androidx.compose.ui.graphics.Color,androidx.compose.ui.graphics.BlendMode,kotlin.Function2)\">rememberVectorPainter</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/ui/graphics/vector/VectorProperty\">VectorProperty</a></code>, <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/ui/graphics/vector/VectorConfig\">VectorConfig</a></code>, and <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/ui/graphics/vector/package-summary#RenderVectorGroup(androidx.compose.ui.graphics.vector.VectorGroup,kotlin.collections.Map)\">RenderVectorGroup</a></code> </li> </li> \n    </ul> <h2>New experimental APIs</h2> <p> We’re continuing to bring new features to Compose. Here are a few highlights: </p> \n    <ul> \n     <li><code>AnimatedContent</code> can now be saved and restored when using <code>rememberSaveable</code>. <li><code>LazyColumn/LazyRow</code> item positions can be animated using <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/compose/foundation/lazy/LazyItemScope#(androidx.compose.ui.Modifier).animateItemPlacement(androidx.compose.animation.core.FiniteAnimationSpec)\">Modifier.animateItemPlacement()</a></code>. <li>You can use the new <code>BringIntoView</code> API to send a request to parents so that they scroll to bring an item into view. </li> </li></li> \n    </ul> <p> Try out the new APIs using <code><a href=\"https://developer.android.com/reference/kotlin/androidx/annotation/OptIn\">@OptIn</a></code> and give us feedback! <p> Note: Using Compose 1.1 requires using Kotlin 1.6.10. Check out the <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/releases/compose-kotlin\">Compose to Kotlin Compatibility Map</a> for more information. </p> <p> Wondering what’s next? Check out our <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/jetpack/androidx/compose-roadmap\">updated roadmap</a> to see the features we’re currently thinking about and working on, such as lazy item animations, downloadable fonts, moveable content, and more! </p> <p> Jetpack Compose is <strong>stable, ready for production,</strong> and continues to add the features you’ve been asking us for. We’ve been thrilled to see tens of thousands of apps start using Jetpack Compose in production already and we can’t wait to see what you’ll build! </p> <p> We’re grateful for all of the bug reports and feature requests submitted to our <strong><a href=\"https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/new?component=612128\">issue tracker</a></strong> over the Alphas and Betas - they help us to improve Compose and build the APIs you need. Do continue providing your feedback and help us make Compose better! </p> <p> Happy composing! </p> \n     <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n      <a 16:26:33","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:26:33","title":"Smule Adopts Google’s Oboe to Improve Recording Quality & Completion Rates","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/02/smule-adopts-googles-oboe-to-improve.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\" content=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhsJgTKhUlIb-1X_G1rWQLCxpd0KMmGTUgqUfSNr4__CsxxjiOdJgJHCtgO9dG8mZdwzAHat9HyIcMsvA-fS0o6T0-_ut_Ej74hKfn09AJUPNc3YscwfGG6hqFS-W_oTczgtd1aGNzpCdDDo4b4lrUM3n8OsFKjvslqE6pHRY3w0aZSTHsaYytSnQSA\"> \n <img style=\"display:none\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhsJgTKhUlIb-1X_G1rWQLCxpd0KMmGTUgqUfSNr4__CsxxjiOdJgJHCtgO9dG8mZdwzAHat9HyIcMsvA-fS0o6T0-_ut_Ej74hKfn09AJUPNc3YscwfGG6hqFS-W_oTczgtd1aGNzpCdDDo4b4lrUM3n8OsFKjvslqE6pHRY3w0aZSTHsaYytSnQSA\"> <p><em>Posted by the Smule Engineering team: David Gayle, Chris Manchester, Mark Gills, Trayko Traykov, Randal Leistikow, Mariya Ivanova.</em><p> \n    <center> \n     <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhsJgTKhUlIb-1X_G1rWQLCxpd0KMmGTUgqUfSNr4__CsxxjiOdJgJHCtgO9dG8mZdwzAHat9HyIcMsvA-fS0o6T0-_ut_Ej74hKfn09AJUPNc3YscwfGG6hqFS-W_oTczgtd1aGNzpCdDDo4b4lrUM3n8OsFKjvslqE6pHRY3w0aZSTHsaYytSnQSA\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Light blue graphic with karaoke elements\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEhsJgTKhUlIb-1X_G1rWQLCxpd0KMmGTUgqUfSNr4__CsxxjiOdJgJHCtgO9dG8mZdwzAHat9HyIcMsvA-fS0o6T0-_ut_Ej74hKfn09AJUPNc3YscwfGG6hqFS-W_oTczgtd1aGNzpCdDDo4b4lrUM3n8OsFKjvslqE6pHRY3w0aZSTHsaYytSnQSA\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n    </center> <br> <h3>Executive Summary</h3> <p> As the most downloaded singing app of all time, <a href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.smule.singandroid\">Smule</a> Inc. has been investing on Android to improve the overall audio quality and, more specifically, to reduce latency, i.e. allowing singers to hear their voices in the headset as they perform. The teams specialized in Audio and Video allocated a significant part of 2021 into making the necessary changes to convert the Smule application used by over ten million Android users from using the OpenSL audio API to the Oboe audio library, enabling roughly a 10%+ increase in recording completion rate. </p> <h3> Introduction </h3> <p> Smule Inc. is a leader in karaoke, with an app that helps millions of people sing their favorite songs and share performances daily. The Smule application goes beyond traditional karaoke by focusing on co-creation, offering users the unique opportunity to share music and collaborate with friends, other singers on the platform, and their favorite music artists. Audio quality is paramount, and, in 2020, the Smule team saw potential to enhance the experience on Android. </p> \n     <center> \n      <a href=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEj5TL57hcCKB2JiT5QOXa7oCbY9vXcqSY8dAJR2QpeR4ylI5UHGDM_7sGLG5sl8OQ-C91R6ZD3ojwrnbsdUXRebAWIzY4kixk4COIb0Exe6wjggNaj0fp53WOieF_3DTMxtVhC4mgRNYgvLi_vB5FlBEPwT0KbmZ0kH51k0hTqcee1wDKCDUxfjml3Z\" imageanchor=\"1\"><img style=\"width:100%\" alt=\"Screenshots of Smule karaoke app\" id=\"imgFull\" border=\"0\" src=\"https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/a/AVvXsEj5TL57hcCKB2JiT5QOXa7oCbY9vXcqSY8dAJR2QpeR4ylI5UHGDM_7sGLG5sl8OQ-C91R6ZD3ojwrnbsdUXRebAWIzY4kixk4COIb0Exe6wjggNaj0fp53WOieF_3DTMxtVhC4mgRNYgvLi_vB5FlBEPwT0KbmZ0kH51k0hTqcee1wDKCDUxfjml3Z\" data-original-width=\"1058\" data-original-height=\"714\" /></a>\n     </center><br> <p> Smule’s legacy OpenSL implementation wasn’t well-suited to leverage the blazing-fast hardware of new devices while supporting the diverse devices across its world-wide market. Smule’s development team determined that upgrading the audio system was a necessary and a logical improvement. </p> <h3>Oboe Rollout Strategy</h3> <p> Smule was faced with two possible routes for improvement: directly targeting <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/ndk/guides/audio/aaudio/aaudio\">AAudio</a>, a high-performance Android C audio API introduced in Android O designed for applications that require low latency, or <a href=\"https://developer.android.com/games/sdk/oboe\">Oboe</a>, which wraps both AAudio and OpenSL internally. After careful evaluation, Smule’s development team opted for Oboe’s easy-to-use code base, and broad device compatibility, and robust community support, which achieved the lowest latency and made the best use of the available native audio. </p> <p> The conversion to Oboe represented a significant architectural and technological evolution. As a result, Smule approached the rollout process conservatively, with a planned, gradual release that started with a small selection of device models to d validate quality. Week after week, the team enabled more devices (reverting a limited number of devices exhibiting problems in Oboe back to OpenSL). This incremental, methodical approach helped to minimize risk and allowed the engineering team to handle device-specific issues as they occurred. </p> <h3> Improving the Audio Quality Experience </h3> <p> Smule switched to Oboe to help improve the app experience. They hoped to reduce dramatically audio playback crashes, eliminate issues such as echo and crackling during recording, and reduce audio latency. A <a href=\"https://android-developers.googleblog.com/2021/03/an-update-on-androids-audio-latency.html\">recent article</a> in the Android Developers blog shows that the average latency of the twenty most popular devices decreased from 109 ms in 2017 to 39ms today using Oboe. Whereas a monitoring delay of 109ms is heard as a distinct echo which interferes with live singing, 39ms is beneath the acceptable threshold for real-time applications. The latencies of top devices today are all within 22ms of one another, and this consistency is a big plus. </p> <p> The lift in recording completion rate Smule has seen using Oboe is likely due to this lower latency, allowing singers to hear their voices in the headset as they perform with Smule’s world-class audio effects applied, but without an echo. </p> <p> Using an effective collaborative GitHub portal dedicated to <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe/issues\">Oboe</a>, the Google team played a significant role in Smule’s Oboe integration, providing them with key insights and support. Working together, the two teams were able to launch the largest Oboe deployment to date, reaching millions of active users. The Smule team contributed to addressing some Oboe code issues, and the Google team coordinated with certain mobile device makers to further improve Oboe's compatibility. </p> <br><p><em>Audio quality is of the utmost importance to our community of singers, and we're thankful for our shared commitment to delivering the best possible experience as well as empowering musical creation on Smule. - Eric Dumas, Smule CTO.</em></p><br> <p> Given the massive scale of the operation, it was only natural to face device-specific issues. One notable example was an OS built-in functionality that injected echo sound effects in the raw audio stream, which prevented Smule from correctly applying its own patented DSP algorithms and audio filters. Google’s team came to the rescue, providing lightning fast updates and patches to the library. The process of reporting Oboe issues was straightforward, well defined, and handled in a timely manner by the Google team. </p> <p> Smule overcame other device-specific roadblocks together, including errors with specific chipsets. As an example, when Oboe was asking for mono microphone input, a few devices provided stereo inputs mixed into one fake mono microphone input. Smule created a ticket in <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe\">Oboe’s GitHub</a>, providing examples and reproducing the issue using the Oboe tester app. </p> <p> The Google-developed <a href=\"https://github.com/google/oboe/tree/master/apps/OboeTester/docs\">Oboe tester app</a> was a helpful tool in solving and identifying issues throughout the implementation. It proved especially useful in testing many of the features of Oboe, AAudio, and OpenSL ES, as well as testing Android devices, measuring latency and glitches, and much more. The application offers a myriad of features that can help to simulate almost any audio setup. The Oboe tester can also be used in automation testing, by launching it from a shell script using an Android Intent. Smule relied heavily on the automation testing, given the large number of devices covered in the integration. </p> <p> Once Smule was confident the device-specific issues were resolved and the Oboe audio was stable enough, Smule switched to a wider split testing rollout approach. In just a few weeks, Smule increased the population using Oboe from 10% to 100% percent of the successful devices, which was only possible due to the positive feedback and green KPI metrics Oboe received continuously throughout the release journey. </p> <p> The results speak for themselves. Smule users on Oboe are singing more - it’s as simple as that. Unique karaoke recordings and performance joins, or duets, increased by a whopping <strong>8.07%, </strong>Unique uploads by 3.84%, and song performances were completed by <strong>4.10%</strong> more. Smule has observed in Q3 and Q4 2021 an increase of the recording completion rate by 10%+. </p> <p> Using the <a href=\"https://firebase.google.com/docs/crashlytics\">Firebase Crashlytics</a> tool by Google, Smule has seen a decline in audio-related crashes since the full Oboe release, making the app more stable - even on lower-end devices. Smule’s dedicated customer support team was thrilled to report a <strong>33% </strong>reduction in audio-related complaints, including issues like (unintended) robot voice and echo. </p> <p> The decision to switch to Oboe has paid off in spades. The application is functioning better than ever and Smule is well-equipped to face further advancements in audio and hardware with the updated technology. Most importantly, Smule users are happy and making music, which is what it’s all about. </p>\n        <div class=\"feedflare\"> \n         <a Stable","link":"http://android-developers.googleblog.com/2022/01/android-studio-bumblebee-202111-stable.html","description":"<meta name=\"twitter:image\"
